GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 53.01 REGISTRATION REQUIRED BEFORE DRILLING WELLS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to drill or
construct a well within the municipal limits of the Town of Clayton without
first registering with the Mayor of the town. The registration shall include
disclosure of the location and purpose of the well, its intended term of use
and plan for capping the well.
   (B)   It shall be the duty of the Town Attorney in and for the Town of
Clayton, to restrain and enjoin, in any court having jurisdiction, any person,
firm or corporation commencing or threatening to commence any well within the
town in violation of this section or which threatens to endanger the health,
safety or welfare of the inhabitants of the town.
   (C)   The provisions of this section shall not affect or be binding upon the
town, its successors and assigns, or any other person, firm or corporation
having a lawful franchise of the town, for the purposes of maintaining a water
system.
   (D)   Compliance with the registration requirement of this section shall not
be construed as license or authority to drill, construct or maintain any well
in violation of any other ordinance of the Town of Clayton or in violation of
any statute or regulation of the State of New Mexico or in violation of any
statute or regulation of the United States of America.
(Ord. 598, passed 7-10-1995) Penalty, see §
53.99
MUNICIPAL WATER SERVICE
§ 53.15 WATER SERVICE DEFINED.
   WATER SERVICE is defined as all and any water furnished to any person,
whether metered or not, through any size pipe.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.16 USE AND APPROVAL.
   Water service may be used by the customer for any and all purposes desired;
provided, however, that, in the interests of public health and safety, any and
all services shall be approved by the Water Department Superintendent or the
Town Manager of the Town of Clayton. Such approval shall be given within a
reasonable length of time, provided that the Town of Clayton is furnished with
a complete drawing or print which shows all piping pertaining to the water
system, sewage, and drainage systems that are to be supplied by the service in
question. The approval for the connection will be given if the installation of
the piping and plumbing meets the requirements of the Town of Clayton and the
requirements of the Uniform Plumbing Code of the State of New Mexico, current
edition and as amended from time.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.17 RULES AND REGULATIONS.
   (A)   The Town Clerk of the Town of Clayton and the Town Manager of the Town
of Clayton are hereby directed to prepare from time to time and as conditions
warrant such general rules and regulations as may be necessary, proper, and
reasonable pertaining to:
      (1)   Applications for water service;
      (2)   Contracts for water service;
      (3)   Deposits required;
      (4)   Extension of line for water service;
      (5)   Temporary water service;
      (6)   Requirements relating to customers', water piping and plumbing
related thereto;
      (7)   Billing and collection for water service;
      (8)   Protection of property of the Municipal Water System;
      (9)   Prevention of theft of water;
      (10)   Discontinuance of service for non-payment of accounts, theft of or
prohibited uses of water; and
      (11)   Such other rules and regulations as may be necessary, proper,
reasonable, and expedient for the conduct of the business of the municipal
water system, and not in conflict with this subchapter.
   (B)   Such rules and regulations so prepared shall be effective only after
approval by the Board of Trustees of the Town of Clayton, New Mexico, by
resolution or ordinance, and when so approved, same shall have the full force
and effect of this subchapter, same as if herein incorporated.
   (C)   The Town Clerk of the Town of Clayton, New Mexico shall keep on file
at all times and open to public inspection during all office hours, a full and
complete revised copy of all such approved rules and regulations pertaining to
the municipal water system.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.18 TOWN TO HAVE LIEN.
   (A)   The Town of Clayton shall have a lien upon any lot, subdivision,
tract, or parcel of land within the town and or county where water service is
provided for all legal charges for water furnished by the Municipal Water
System and used upon such lot, subdivision, tract, or parcel of land, or in or
upon which any building, buildings, or structures thereon situated. When any
lot, sub-division, tract, or parcel of land, or any building, buildings or
structures thereon situate, in or upon which water is being used shall become
vacant, it shall be the duty of the owner, agent, or former tenant or tenants
to give notice in writing to the Town Clerk of the Town of Clayton, New Mexico,
that the premises are vacant; and when such notice is so given, no lien for
water furnished after 3 days from receipt of the written notice shall be had
against the said property.
   (B)   Such lien may be enforced by appropriate suit in the District Court of
Union County, New Mexico, in which county the Town of Clayton, New Mexico, is
located.
   (C)   The town shall be entitled to recover its costs and attorney's fees in
such proceedings which are also secured by the lien on the land.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.19 APPLICATION FOR WATER SERVICE.
   (A)   The water service application form must be completed in its entirety.
   (B)   All property owners shall show evidence of ownership.
   (C)   Renters shall provide a copy of written lease or rental agreement.
   (D)   Applicants for new water service must pay the cost of the water
service, which would include labor, use of machinery and all materials up to
the meter.
   (E)   After application and the proper deposit is made, water service will
be made within a reasonable time, the same day, if no line extension or new
service is required; and if such line extension and new service is required,
service will be given as soon as possible.
   (F)   No excavation or tie-in shall be made by a water customer or his
contractor until approval is given by the town.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.20 DEPOSITS.
   All applicants for water service will pay a flat fee deposit of $75.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.21 CONTRACTS FOR WATER SERVICE.
   Contracts for water service are necessary if such service requires line
extension and/or a new service line. Such contracts are to be made and approved
by the Board of Trustees if such an extension requires more than 100 feet of
main extension, or up to 100 feet of main line and for any service larger than
1-1/2 inches.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.22 TEMPORARY WATER SERVICE.
   The total cost of temporary service, including line extension, valves,
fittings, and pipe; taking out of that part of the temporary service, including
the use of machinery, labor, and loss due to that part of the fitting that
would necessarily need be left in the main line; water used per month according
to the applicable rate; all to be paid for as a temporary service.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.23 PIPING AND PLUMBING.
   All customer piping and related plumbing shall conform with the requirements
of the Uniform Plumbing Code current edition.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.24 BILLING AND COLLECTING.
   Billing and collecting for water service shall be as provided in this
subchapter. No adjustments will be made to the amount of water used. Due to
leaks or freezing and bursting.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.25 PROTECTION OF PROPERTY OF THE CLAYTON MUNICIPAL WATER SYSTEM.
   (A)   If any trouble should exist on any of the municipal water mains,
service lines, wells, reservoir, and meters, the Municipal Water Department is
to be notified. No person other than Municipal Water Department employees are
to work on, repair, make taps, or any other necessary repairs and additions.
   (B)   Pipes, service, main lines, meters, or any other part of the municipal
water system, torn, mutilated by contractor or any person, must be reported
immediately; and upon full repair, such person, firm, or contractor shall pay
full cost of repair.
   (C)   Fire plugs damaged by vehicles or persons shall be reported
immediately; and upon repair, such person responsible shall pay cost of repair.
   (D)   Any property owner, renter, or user of water from the municipal water
system that attempts to thaw out a frozen meter or a meter that he thinks is
frozen, by fire of any source, and damages the water meter, shall pay the full
cost of the meter repairs. These persons should call the Clayton Municipal
Water Department Office and report such stoppage of water before attempting to
thaw out a meter.
   (E)   Any person, firm, or contractor that drives any vehicle over any meter
water box breaking same, shall report such damage, and after repairs, pay for
the cost of such damage.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.26 PREVENTION OF THEFT OF WATER.
   (A)   Each water service of any size has a stop in the service line, either
a curb stop, or a valve. If such stop or valve is closed off by representatives
of the municipal water system, such valves are not to be opened by anyone until
the proper application and deposits are made.
   (B)   Damaging a water meter or water meter dial or breaking the glass on a
water meter dial shall be paid for by person damaging same.
   (C)   Breaking or damaging water meter box locks shall be paid for by the
person responsible.
   (D)   No person, other than Municipal Water Department employees and
licensed plumbers, should attempt to open a water meter box or turn off a
service valve that is in the water system of any service. Anyone breaking such
valve or meter must pay cost of new valve.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.27 DISCONTINUANCE OF SERVICE FOR NON-PAYMENT OF ACCOUNTS, THEFT OF, OR
PROHIBITED USE OF WATER.
   (A)   Thirty days after the water bill is submitted, and the bill is not
paid, then on the 31st day said service shall be disconnected for non-payment
of bill.
   (B)   If any person or customer has been proven of the theft of water, then
the manager of the municipal water system shall order discontinuance of service
until the town is aid for the water used.
   (C)   When water service shall be reconnected only upon payment of all
arrearages, penalties, and accrued charges and in addition thereto payment of a
$75 reconnect fee and a deposit in double the amount specified for new service.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720,
passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.28 ADDITIONAL RULES AND REGULATIONS.
   Any person loitering around wells or reservoirs, or permitting animals to be
around any reservoir, will be notified to stop same and if the procedure is not
stopped immediately, then he or she will be apprehended to protect the safety
of the water supply to the town.
(Ord. 653, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 685, passed 12-14-2011)
RATES AND CHARGES
§ 53.40 RATES AND HOOKUP CHARGES.
   (A)   Except otherwise specified in this section, water service rates are
hereby set at a minimum and for the first 2,000 gallons use at $29.04 as of
July 1, 2023; $31.94 as of July 1, 2024; and shall increase at the rate of 10%
per year on July 1, of each year thereafter through the year 2027. All water
used above 2,000 gallons per month shall be billed per 1,000 gallons used.
$2.66 as of July 1, 2023; $2.93 as of July 1, 2024; and shall increase at the
rate of 10% per year on July 1, of each year thereafter through the year 2027.
   (B)   The rate for water pumped directly from the tanks and the rate for
water used by a prison, correctional facility or jail are a minimum and for
each 1,000 gallons used $6.65 as of July 1, 2023; $7.31 as of July 1, 2024; and
shall increase at the rate of 10% per year on July 1, of each year thereafter
through the year 2027.
   (C)   The rates for water used at a golf course are a minimum and for the
first 2,000 gallons used $1.27 as of July 1, 2023; $1.40 as of July 1, 2024;
and shall increase at the rate of 10% per year on July l, of each year
thereafter. All water used above 2,000 gallons per month shall be per 1,000
gallons, $0.90 as of July 1, 2023; $0.99 per 1,000 gallons as of July 1, 2024;
and shall increase at the rate of 10% per year on July 1, of each year
thereafter through the year 2027.
(Ord. 654, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 660, passed 7-17-2008; Am. Ord. 686,
passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720, passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.41 ACCOUNTS, BILLING, AND PAYMENT.
   (A)   All accounts for water service furnished by the Town of Clayton
Municipal Water System under the schedule designated in this ordinance are due
and payable at the office of the Town Clerk of the Town of Clayton, New Mexico,
upon date of billing.
   (B)   On any bill unpaid by the due date, following billing date, or 10 days
from date of billing, 10% will be added as a late penalty.
(Ord. 654, passed 9-14-2006; Am. Ord. 660, passed 7-17-2008; Am. Ord. 686,
passed 12-14-2011; Am. Ord. 720, passed 5-10-2023)
§ 53.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person, firm or corporation violating the provisions of division
(A) of §
53.01 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction thereof,
shall be fined a sum not to exceed $300 or shall be imprisoned for not more
than 90 days, or shall receive both the fine and imprisonment.
   (C)   (1)   It shall be unlawful and a violation of §§
53.15 through
53.27, 53.40 and 53.41 to do or cause to be done any of the following:
         (a)   Remove locking lid from meter can;
         (b)   Tamper with radio receiver on lid; or
         (c)   Tamper with water meter.
      (2)   Any person in violation of § 53.040 and has caused damage to
property owned by the Town of Clayton Water Department shall be fined not less
than $250 and no more than $500 or imprisoned for a term of not less than 1 day
in the City County Jail nor more than a term of 90 days. The use of Uniform
traffic citations are authorized for any enforcement of this section.
(Ord. 598, passed 7-10-1995; Am. Ord. 720, passed 5-10-2023)
CHAPTER 54: ELECTRICITY
Section
   
54.01   Hearing to protest elimination of electrical services
Cross-reference:
   Radio aerials and the like attached to electric utility poles, see §
90.03
§ 54.01 HEARING TO PROTEST ELIMINATION OF ELECTRICAL SERVICES.
   (A)   Utility service; seriously ill individuals. Utility service shall not
be discontinued to any residence where a seriously ill person is residing, if
the person responsible for the utility service charges does not have the
financial resources to pay the charges, and if a practitioner of the healing of
arts, as defined in paragraph 2 of subsection (B) of NMSA § 59A-22-32(B),
certifies that the discontinuance of service might endanger that person’s life
and the certificate is delivered to a manager or officer of the utility
providing the service at least 2 days prior to the due date of a billing for
utility services. The Public Service Commission shall provide, by rules and
regulations, the procedure necessary to carry out this section.
   (B)   Statement required.
      (1)   Customers of the town electric utility service may appeal the
discontinuance of electric service for nonpayment of the electric service bill.
      (2)   The customer must present or mail a written statement, signed by
the customer, stating why the electric utility service should not be
discontinued.
      (3)   In the event no signed, written statement is received by the Town
Office within 5 days of the date of the final notice, the town may discontinue
services.
   (C)   Hearing, proof and result.
      (1)   Upon receipt of a signed written statement of reasons why a town
electric utility customer’s service should not be discontinued, the Municipal
Court shall set a hearing time and date.
      (2)   The hearing time and date set shall be as soon as practicable after
receipt of the signed written statement and in no event more than 5 working
days after receipt of the signed written statement.
      (3)   The town shall prove by a preponderance of the evidence that the
electric bill is due and payable.
      (4)   The customer of the town electric services shall have the burden of
proving by a preponderance of the evidence that the electric bill protested is
incorrect, paid in full or not due and payable.
      (5)   The Municipal Court Judge shall have no authority to compromise,
set off, abate or forgive any electric service charges owed to the town.
      (6)   In the event the town prevails in the Municipal Court hearing on
the termination of electric utility service, the Mayor shall order the
discontinuance of electric services for nonpayment immediately.
(Ord. 522, passed 2-11-1980)
CHAPTER 55: GAS
Section
Installation, Use and Maintenance of Equipment
Using Gas for Heat, Light and Power
   
55.01   Curb valves
   
55.02   Location of burners
   
55.03   Connections
   
55.04   Protection from stoves
   
55.05   Gasoline hazard
   
55.06   Tests
   
55.07   Stove pipe chimneys
   
55.08   Certificate of inspection; setting of meters
   
55.09   Warning after shut-off
   
55.10   Proximity to electrical wiring
   
55.11   Quality of materials
   
55.12   Cutting timbers
   
55.13   Use of matches, candles and flames
   
55.14   Additional inspections
   
55.15   Size of pipes
 
   
55.99   Penalty
INSTALLATION, USE AND MAINTENANCE OF EQUIPMENT
USING GAS FOR HEAT, LIGHT AND POWER
§ 55.01 CURB VALVES.
   Every building in which gas is used shall have each supply pipe leading from
the street mains provided with a heavy brass straightway stopcock or valve,
placed at or near the curb or property line and arranged to permit shutting off
at that point.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)
§ 55.02 LOCATION OF BURNERS.
   All gas burners shall be placed at least 3 feet below any woodwork or
ceiling attached to wooden beams, unless the same is properly protected by a
shield, in which case the distance shall be not less than 18 inches. No gas
bracket on any lath and plaster partition of woodwork shall be less than 6
inches in length, measured from the burner to the platter surface or woodwork.
Gas lights placed near window curtains or other combustible material shall be
guarded by globes or wire cages.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)
§ 55.03 CONNECTIONS.
   Gas connections to stoves and similar heating devices shall be made by rigid
metal pipes. For small portable heating devices, if a rigid connection is
necessarily impractical, flexible metal or rubber tubing may be used when there
is a valve or other shut-off on the intake end of the tubing and the tubing is
securely clamped in place at both ends.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)
§ 55.04 PROTECTION FROM STOVES.
   All gas, gasoline, oil or charcoal burning stoves or heating devices shall
be placed on iron stands at least 6 inches above combustible supports unless
the burners are at least 5 inches above the base with metal guard plates 4
inches below the burners.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)
§ 55.05 GASOLINE HAZARD.
   No open flame or heating device shall be used in any room where gasoline or
other volatile inflammable fluids are stored or handled.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928) Penalty, see §
55.99
§ 55.06 TESTS.
   After all piping is installed and all outlets capped, there shall be applied
by the workers installing the equipment, in the presence of the Inspector of
plumbing or a deputy, a test with air under pressure sufficient to support a
column of mercury 12 inches in height, which shall stand for 10 minutes. Only a
mercury gauge shall be used. No piping shall be covered, nor shall any fixture,
gas heater or range be connected thereto, until a card showing the approval of
this test has been issued by the Inspector.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)
§ 55.07 STOVE PIPE CHIMNEYS.
   The use of metal stove pipes or stacks passing through combustible floors,
partitions, ceilings, walls or roofs is prohibited. When any gas appliance is
directly connected into a flue, the flue must be constructed of brick, concrete
or tile.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)
§ 55.08 CERTIFICATE OF INSPECTION; SETTING OF METERS.
   No meter shall be set by any gas company until a certificate is filed with
them from the Inspector certifying that the gas pipes and fixtures comply with
the provisions of this and other ordinances pertaining thereto.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)
§ 55.09 WARNING AFTER SHUT-OFF.
   No person, firm or individual shall resume service or turn gas into mains
which have been shut- off temporarily or for any length of time until all
consumers using gas from the mains have been notified of the resumption of
service and have been warned to close all outlets left open when the service
was interrupted.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928) Penalty, see §
55.99
§ 55.10 PROXIMITY TO ELECTRICAL WIRING.
   No gas piping will be permitted closer than 6 inches to any electric wiring
exposed.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)
§ 55.11 QUALITY OF MATERIALS.
   (A)   Pipe used shall be standard, full weight, of the best quality of
wrought iron or steel and free from defects. All fittings (except stopcocks and
valves) shall be of best quality malleable iron; no cast iron fittings shall be
used.
   (B)   Nipples and reducing couplings must be used; in no case shall bushings
be used.
   (C)   All pipe shall be reamed after cutting.
   (D)   All piping shall be so installed that it is not subjected to
unnecessary strain and shall be supported by metal straps or hangers where
necessary.
   (E)   No cement of any kind shall be used to repair faulty fittings.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)
§ 55.12 CUTTING TIMBERS.
   (A)   When, in running pipe, it is necessary to cross wood joists or beams,
they shall not be notched to a depth of more than 1/5 of the depth of the
timber, and the notching shall in no case be further from a support than 1/6 of
the total unsupported span of the timber.
   (B)   Where feasible, the piping shall be run so that only timbers having
the shortest spans shall be cut.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)
§ 55.13 USE OF MATCHES, CANDLES AND FLAMES.
   No matches, candles or flames or other sources of ignition shall be used by
a gas fitter, plumber or helper when working on meters, piping or appliances
filled with gas, except for the work as necessarily involves the use of the
flames. A flame shall never be used in searching for leaks.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928) Penalty, see §
55.99
§ 55.14 ADDITIONAL INSPECTIONS.
   The Inspector of Plumbing, or his or her duly authorized deputy, shall from
time to time, as he or she deems proper, inspect the gas fixtures and
appliances in any building and shall make the requirements relating thereto as
he or she may deem the public health and safety require, and the owner, agent
or occupant of the buildings shall comply with the requirements. Any additional
piping installed after an inspection certificate is issued must be reported for
inspection when completed.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)
§ 55.15 SIZE OF PIPES.
   No pipe to supply gas to any consumer shall be smaller than hereinafter
specified:
   (A)   From street or alley opening to meter, l-1/4 inch;
   (B)   For 1 opening, l-1/4 inch pipe to the point of opening;
   (C)   For 2 openings, 1-1/4 inch pipe to first opening and 1-inch pipe to
the second opening;
   (D)   For 3 openings, 1-1/4 inch pipe to the first opening, 1-inch pipe to
the second opening and 3/4-inch pipe to the third opening;
   (E)   For 4 openings, 1-1/4 inch pipe to the first opening, 1-inch pipe to
the second opening, and 3/4-inch pipe to the third and fourth openings;
   (F)   For 5 openings, 1-1/4 inch pipe to the first opening, 1-inch pipe to
the second and third openings and 3/4-inch pipe to the fourth and fifth
openings;
   (G)   For 6 openings, 1-1/4 inch pipe to the point of second opening, 1-inch
pipe to the third and fourth openings and 3/4-inch pipe to the fifth and sixth
openings;
   (H)   For 7 openings, 1-1/4 inch pipe to the point of the second opening, 1-
inch pipe to the point to the fifth opening and 3/4-inch pipe to the sixth and
seventh openings;
   (I)   For 8 openings, 1-inch pipe to the point of the third opening, 1-inch
pipe to the point of the sixth opening and 3/4-inch pipe to the seventh and
eighth openings; and
   (J)   When more than 8 openings are to be installed the installation, shall
be as prescribed by the Inspector of Plumbing in each case.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)
§ 55.99 PENALTY.
   Any person, firm or corporation who shall fail to comply with any of the
provisions of this chapter or who shall violate any of its provisions, shall,
upon conviction thereof, be punished by a fine of not less than $5 nor more
than $50. Each 10 days or major fraction thereof during which any unlawful
condition is permitted to continue by the responsible person shall be deemed a
separate offense.
(Ord. 169, passed 8-27-1928)

70.03   State transportation regulations; adopted by reference
§ 70.01 NEW MEXICO MOTOR VEHICLE CODE; ADOPTED BY REFERENCE.
   (A)   The New Mexico Motor Vehicle Code, including the 2001 amendments
thereto as codified at NMSA §§ 66-1-1 through 66-1-5 and 66-7-1 through 66-8-
137, is hereby adopted by reference, subject to the provisions of division (B)
below, and incorporated herein as if set out in full.
   (B)   No offense which would constitute a felony or a high court misdemeanor
or Driving While Intoxicated or Driving Under the Influence of Alcohol or
Intoxicating Drugs is hereby adopted, and all such offenses are excepted from
this section.
   (C)   Effective date of this section is October 1, 2001.
(Ord. 562, passed 6-27-1988; Am. Ord. 620, passed 9-11-2001)
§ 70.02 NEW MEXICO UNIFORM TRAFFIC ORDINANCE; ADOPTED BY REFERENCE.
   The 2011 Compilation of the New Mexico Uniform Traffic Ordinance, comprising
NMSA §§ 12-1-1 through 12-13-6 inclusive, and all changes through July 1, 2017,
are herewith adopted by reference, pursuant to NMSA § 3-17-6.
(Ord. 656, passed 11-13-2007; Am. Ord. 672, passed 2-22-2010; Am. Ord. 675,
passed 9-15-2010; Am. Ord. 682, passed 9-14-2011; Am. Ord. 699, passed 8-22-
2017)
§ 70.03 STATE TRANSPORTATION REGULATIONS; ADOPTED BY REFERENCE.
   (A)   Adoption. The following state legislation from the 1978 compilation
regarding transportation and motor carriers is hereby adopted by reference as
if set out in full herein:
      (1)   The New Mexico Motor Transportation Act, being NMSA Article 65-1 et
seq.;
      (2)   The New Mexico Motor Carriers Act, being NMSA Article 65-2 et seq.;
      (3)   The New Mexico Motor Carriers Safety Act, being NMSA Article 65-
3 et seq.;
      (4)   The New Mexico Motor Carriers Transportation Agents Act, being NMSA
Article 65-4 et seq.; and
      (5)   Procedures for vehicles entering or leaving the state, being NMSA
Article 65-5 et seq.
   (B)   Whenever any of the above mentioned laws direct the payment of any
fine, penalty or assessment, the same shall be payable to the Town of Clayton,
New Mexico.
   (C)   Whenever any of the above laws direct that a magistrate having
jurisdiction of any offense shall act, the Municipal Court of the town shall
also be authorized to so act.
   (D)   Copies of the above listed laws shall be available for inspection
during the normal and regular business hours of the town at the town offices,
from 9:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m., Monday through Friday. Copies of the above
mentioned laws shall be available upon request and payment of a charge of $100.
(Ord. 562, passed 6-27-1988)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 71.01 RESERVED.
§ 71.02 PROHIBITING ENGINE BRAKING DEVICES OR RETARDERS.
   No device commonly known as a Jacobs engine brake or engine retarder or
engine brake shall be operated within the municipal limits of the Town of
Clayton.
(Ord. 597, passed 7-10-1995) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.03 ADEQUATE BRAKES; HONKING RESTRICTED.
   (A)   Proper equipment. Every motor vehicle when operated within the Town of
Clayton shall be equipped with brakes adequate to control the movement of and
to stop and hold the vehicle and shall be equipped with a horn or other warning
device, and shall have a valid inspection certificate on the vehicle, and shall
be properly equipped with muffler or other equipment that will do away with
unnecessary noises.
   (B)   Excessive honking. No person shall engage in excessive or unnecessary
honking of the horn on any motor vehicle within the town.
(Ord. 304, passed 12-9-1946; Am. Ord. 434, passed 8-8-1966) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.04 DESIGNATED AUTHORIZED EMERGENCY VEHICLES.
   The following vehicles are designated as authorized emergency vehicles
pursuant to the provision of NMSA § 66-1-4.1(E):
   (A)   The 2 police cars regularly operated by the Police Department of the
Town of Clayton and any substitute vehicles used for the purposes;
   (B)   The 4 Fire Department pumper trucks used by the Fire Department of the
Town of Clayton; and
   (C)   The emergency panel truck used by the Fire Department of the Town of
Clayton.
(Ord. 444, passed 7-8-1968)
§ 71.05 SPEED RESTRICTIONS IN FIRE ZONE AND OTHER PLACES OF TOWN DURING CERTAIN
HOURS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a motor vehicle within the
Fire Zone of the Town of Clayton at a speed greater than 20 mph, or to operate
a motor vehicle upon any alley of the town at a speed greater than 10 mph, or
to operate a motor vehicle within a school or hospital zone, that is, within ½
block of either a public school or a hospital, at a speed greater than 15 mph
(provided, however, the restriction as to schools shall apply only to the
school period, which period is designated as between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and
4:00 p.m., and only on those days when school is actually in session), or to
operate a motor vehicle at a speed in excess of 25 mph upon other streets of
the town and through school zones at times when the above special restriction
shall not be applicable.
(Ord. 304, passed 12-9-1946) Penalty, see §
71.99
Cross-reference:
   Hospital quiet zone, see §
71.08
§ 71.06 U TURNS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for the driver of any motor vehicle to make a “U
turn”, that is, to reverse the direction of travel of the vehicle, except at a
street intersection. U turns shall not be made at the intersections of Main and
Front Street, Main and First Streets, Main and Second Streets, Main and Third
Streets, First and Chestnut Streets and First and Walnut Streets.
   (B)   U turns shall not be made at the intersection of Main Street and
Railroad Avenue or at any point between the intersections of Main and Front
Street and Main and Railroad Avenue.
(Ord. 304, passed 12-9-1946; Am. Ord. 330, passed 5-9-1949; Am. Ord. 373,
passed 1-11-1956) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.07 STOP INTERSECTIONS.
   Stop intersections shall be as set forth in
Chapter 74, Schedule III.
(Ord. 304, passed 12-9-1946; Am. Ord. 306, passed 8-25-1947; Am. Ord. 330,
passed 5-9-1949)
§ 71.08 QUIET ZONES.
   (A)   There is hereby established a quiet zone on Jefferson, Harding and
Wilson Streets, and Third and Fourth Avenues, within 1 block of the Union
County Hospital, which is located in Block No. 656 of the Herzstein and Hill
Addition to the Town of Clayton, New Mexico, at the intersection of Harding
Street and Third Avenue. The Town Engineer is hereby authorized, empowered and
directed to erect suitable signs on all of the streets and avenues at a point 1
complete block removed from the hospital site giving appropriate warning of the
quiet zone and of the speed limit therein as hereinafter established at 15 mph.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any operator of any motor vehicle, except
emergency, fire, police or ambulance vehicles, to sound any horn, klaxon,
siren, cut out or other noise producing mechanism within the quiet zone so
established by the signs.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a motor vehicle within
the quiet zone as defined herein and as established by the signs, except
emergency, police, ambulance or fire vehicles at a speed greater than 15 mph.
(Ord. 411, passed 8-13-1962) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.09 RAILROADS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any engineer or conductor or any person
having charge, either permanently or temporarily, of any railroad engine, train
or car or cars, to run any engine or train or permit the same to run within the
Town of Clayton without ringing the engine bell and sounding the whistle, or at
a greater rate of speed while crossing street crossings than 25 mph, and both
engineer and conductor shall be liable for the same offense.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any railroad engineer, conductor, yard
master, agent or any other railroad employee having charge, either permanently
or temporarily, of any railway engine, train, car or cars, to allow, suffer or
permit any railway engine, train, car or cars to come to a stop and stand or
remain standing across Twentieth Street in the town, or upon any part of the
street for more than 2 minutes, or across or upon Twenty-First Street for a
longer period than 5 minutes, or upon any other street or open road within the
town limits, for a longer period than 10 minutes at any 1 time, except it be in
case of unavoidable accident or casualty, and except it be a passenger train.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful for any minor not in the regular employment of
any railroad company to get upon freight or other cars in the town for the
purpose of braking or riding on the same, or for any other purpose except as a
passenger coming or going from the station in the town.
(Ord. 13, passed 6-10-1908; Am. Ord. 44, passed 1-10-1910; Am. Ord. 212, passed
2-9-1931) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.10 PROHIBITING TEXTING WHILE DRIVING.
   (A)   A person shall not read or view a text message or manually type on a
handheld mobile communication device for any purpose while driving a motor
vehicle, except to summon medical or other emergency help or unless that device
is an amateur radio and the driver holds a valid amateur radio operator license
issued by the federal communications commission.
   (B)   The provisions of this section shall not be construed as authorizing
the seizure or forfeiture of a handheld mobile communication device. Unless
otherwise provided by law, the handheld mobile communication device used in the
violation of the provisions of this section is not subject to search by a law
enforcement officer during a traffic stop made pursuant to the provisions of
this section.
   (C)   As used in this section:
      DRIVING. Being in actual physical control of a motor vehicle on a highway
or street and includes being temporarily stopped because of traffic, a traffic
light or stop sign or otherwise, but DRIVING excludes operating a motor vehicle
when the vehicle has pulled over to the side of or off of an active roadway and
has stopped at a location in which it can safely remain stationary.
      HANDHELD MOBILE COMMUNICATION DEVICE. A wireless communication device
that is designed to receive and transmit text or image messages, but HANDHELD
MOBILE COMMUNICATION DEVICE excludes global positioning or navigation systems,
devices that are physically or electronically integrated into a motor vehicle
and voice-operated or hands-free devices that allow the user to compose, send
or read a text message without the use of a hand except to activate or
deactivate or initiate a feature or function.
      TEXT MESSAGE. A digital communication transmitted or intended to be
transmitted between communication devices and includes electronic mail, an
instant message, a text or image communication and a command or request to an
internet site; but "text message" excludes communications through the use of a
computer-aided dispatch service by law enforcement or rescue personnel.
   (D)   The penalty for violation of this section shall be a fine of up to
$500.
(Ord. 693, passed 10-14-2014)
MOTOR VEHICLES AND AIRPORT RUNWAYS
§ 71.20 PROHIBITING MOTOR VEHICLES, MOTORCYCLES AND THE LIKE ON AIRPORT
RUNWAYS.
   It shall be unlawful and a violation of this section for any person to

personnel of the Town of Clayton upon the established and defined runways of
the Municipal Airport, both paved and grass, airport taxiways and apron areas
except in those areas designated for the operation of motor vehicles. It shall
also be a violation of this section to operate motor vehicles, motorcycles and
other vehicles in areas adjacent to or near airport runways, taxiways and apron
areas except on those clearly established presently existing roadways serving
those areas.

STREET USE OF TRUCKS AND TRAILERS; LICENSE/PERMITS REQUIRED
§ 71.35 UNLAWFUL TO CONVEY IN TRUCK WITHOUT PERMIT.
   It is hereby declared unlawful for any person to use the streets of the town
or any vacant lot or public place therein, for the purpose of conveying thereon
by truck, or by truck with trailer, any goods, wares and merchandise whatsoever
for sale to the inhabitants of the town in any public place within the town
other than within a building therein, unless a license or temporary permit
therefor shall have been issued by the town as provided in this subchapter.
(Ord. 309, passed 2-2-1948) Penalty, see §
71.99
§ 71.36 LICENSE FEES.
   License fees for each truck as a separate unit, or for each truck and
trailer therewith, considered as a unit, shall be as follows:
   (A)   For each truck as a separate unit, or a truck and the trailer
therewith considered as a unit, annually, $50; and
   (B)   For a temporary 3-month permit, $12.50.
(Ord. 309, passed 2-2-1948)
§ 71.37 REQUIRED INFORMATION FOR LICENSE OR PERMIT.
   Each license or temporary permit shall contain the following information:
   (A)   The name and address of the licensee or permittee;
   (B)   The license number of the truck, or license numbers of the truck and
trailer (if issued for 2 vehicles as a unit); and
   (C)   The engine number of the truck, or if issued for 2 vehicles, the
engine number of the truck and serial number of the trailer for which issued,
together with the make and model number of each vehicle covered by the license
or permit.
(Ord. 309, passed 2-2-1948)
§ 71.38 DISPLAYING OF LICENSE OR PERMIT.
   The license or permit shall be prominently displayed upon the inside of the
windshield of each truck so licensed at all times during which the goods, wares
and merchandise shall be offered or displayed for sale at any public place
within the Town of Clayton.
(Ord. 309, passed 2-2-1948)
§ 71.39 EXPIRATION OF LICENSES.
   All the annual licenses shall expire on December 31 next following their
issuance, and all temporary permits shall expire respectively on March 31, June
30, September 30 and December 31 next following their issuance: the temporary
permits being issued for 3 calendar months only in each year.
(Ord. 309, passed 2-2-1948)
§ 71.40 INSPECTION OF TRUCKS AND TRAILERS.
   The Town Marshal, or any police officer of the town, is hereby designated as
Inspector to examine trucks and trailers for the above specified purposes. It
shall be his or her duty to see that each license or temporary permit is
prominently displayed inside the cab of each truck upon the windshield thereof.
Should the Inspector observe that any truck, or truck and trailer, so licensed
is being used to display any of the goods, wares and merchandise for sale under
the circumstances as shall constitute in his or her judgment a fraud upon the
citizens of the town, it shall be his or her duty to report the same to the
Mayor, who shall in his or her discretion report the same to the Board of
Trustees, which shall, after 5 days’ notice in writing of the hearing sent
through the United States mail to the address of the licensee or permittee
shown in his or her application for the license, in its discretion revoke any
license or temporary permit.
(Ord. 309, passed 2-2-1948)
§ 71.41 APPLICATIONS.
   All applications for any license or temporary permit hereafter issued under
this subchapter shall be made by the applicant under oath, stating all facts to
be included in the license or temporary permit.
(Ord. 309, passed 2-2-1948)
§ 71.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   (1)   Any person violating any ordinance relating to the operation of
a motor vehicle for which a penalty assessment schedule has been established,
and who chooses to pay the penalty assessment, shall pay in addition to the
penalty assessment a penalty assessment fee of $5.
      (2)   All penalty assessment fees, collected above and beyond the penalty
assessment, shall be deposited in a special fund in the Municipal Treasury and
shall be used solely for the purpose of constructing, operating or maintaining
the municipal jail or for paying the cost of housing municipal prisoners in the
county jail.
(Ord. 543, passed 6-27-1983)
   (C)   Any person, firm or corporation who violates §
71.02 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall
be fined not more than $300 or shall be imprisoned not more than 90 days, or
shall receive both the fine and the imprisonment.
(Ord. 597, passed 7-10-1995)
   (D)   Any person convicted of violation of any provision of §
71.08 shall be deemed guilty of an offense, and punished by a fine of not more
than $200 or imprisonment for not more than 30 days.
(Ord. 411, passed 8-13-1962)
   (E)   Anyone found to be in violation of §
71.20 shall be fined not more than $100 or imprisoned for not more than 10
days, or both.
(Ord. 503, passed 2-28-1977)
   (F)   Any person convicted of violation of any provision of §
71.21 shall be deemed guilty of an ordinance violation, and punished by a fine
of not more than $200 or imprisonment for not more than 90 days, in the
discretion of the court.
(Ord. 418, passed 12-9-1963)
   (G)   The violation of §§
71.35 through

by a fine not exceeding $100 or imprisonment not exceeding 60 days, or both the
fine and imprisonment.
(Ord. 309, passed 2-2-1948)
CHAPTER 72: BICYCLES AND RECREATIONAL VEHICLES

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 72.01 BICYCLE ROUTES IN TOWN.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context indicates or requires a different
meaning.
      BICYCLE. Any mechanical device propelled solely by the power produced
from the exertion of muscles by the person riding and operating the device,
irrespective of the number of wheels thereon.
      BIKE ROUTE. That portion of a shared roadway approximately 4 feet in
width, located approximately 8 feet from the curb of the roadway, which is duly
designated by the Chief of Police, the Mayor and the ad hoc Bicycle Committee,
as a bicycle route, after publication of the proposed route, at least 7 days
prior to the designation thereof. The BIKE ROUTE is to be marked and striped in
accord with the regulations of the New Mexico State Highway Department, as such
are in effect at the time of the establishment of the BIKE ROUTE.
      MOTOR VEHICLE. Any mechanical device operated upon the streets or
highways of the Town of Clayton, which is propelled by any other means than the
muscle power of the person operating it, including wind driven machines and
electrically motivated machines as well as all devices propelled by means of
any type of internal combustion engine.
   (B)   Bike routes. There shall be established from time to time within the
Town of Clayton, along streets duly designated as provided in the definition
above, bike routes. The bike routes shall be at least 4 feet in width and shall
be located not less than 8 feet from the curb of the town street on streets
within residential areas; on thoroughfares within the Town of Clayton on which
parking of motor vehicles is not permitted or does not occur, the bicycle lane
of the bike route shall occupy the 4 feet adjacent to the outside or curb edge
of the pavement on the street.
   (C)   Motor vehicles on bike routes. It shall be a violation of this section
for any person to operate a motor vehicle within a bike route as such is duly
established and marked within the Town of Clayton when the bike route is being
used by a bicycle. Operation of a motor vehicle within the bike route area
during such times as the motor vehicle is not closer than 50 feet to any
bicycle being operated within the bike route shall not constitute a violation
of this section. Operating a motor vehicle to cross a bike route for the
purpose of parking or entering the roadway, shall not constitute a violation of
this section as long as it is done in the manner as to not pose any hazard to
the operators of bicycles when using the bike route. Motor vehicles shall at
all times yield the use of the bike route area, as established and marked, to
bicycles.
   (D)   Use of bicycle lane. Persons operating bicycles on roadways which
include shared roadway and a bicycle lane thereon are encouraged to use the
bicycle lane, but are not required to do so. It shall be a violation of this
section for a bicyclist to use the bike route to travel in opposition to the
prevailing traffic flow for that side of the street. The bike route shall be at
all times used to move in the same direction as the flow of motor vehicular
traffic for that side of the street. This division (D) shall not apply to bike
paths adjacent to a roadway.
(Ord. 504, passed 7-11-1977) Penalty, see §
72.99
REGULATIONS OF MOTORCYCLES, SCOOTERS AND THE LIKE
§ 72.15 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context indicates or requires a different meaning.
   MOTORCYCLE. Every motor vehicle having a seat or saddle for the use of the
rider and designed to travel on not more than 3 wheels in contact with the
ground, but excluding a tractor.
   MOTOR-DRIVEN CYCLES. Every motorcycle, including every motor scooter with a
motor which produces not to exceed 5 horsepower, and every bicycle with motor
attached.
(Ord. 431, passed 9-13-1965)
§ 72.16 SCOPE OF ORDINANCE.
   Every motorcycle, motor-driven cycle, motor scooter and every bicycle with
motor attached shall be deemed included in this subchapter and are hereinafter
referred to as VEHICLE.
(Ord. 431, passed 9-13-1965)
§ 72.17 EQUIPMENT REQUIRED.
   Every vehicle shall be equipped with suitable electrical lights, including
not more than 2 head lamps, a tail light, a tail light reflector and a stop
lamp on every new vehicle sold in New Mexico from and after January 1, 1954,
meeting the requirements of NMSA §§ 66-3-801 through 66-3-887, as amended, a
brake or brakes, a horn, a muffler and a rear-vision mirror, all in good
working order, the requirements of the statutes being included in this
subchapter by this express reference insofar as they relate to vehicles covered
by this subchapter; in particular, every muffler of the vehicle shall be in
good working order and in constant operation to prevent excessive or unusual
noise, and no person shall use a muffler, cut-out, bypass or similar device
upon any vehicle on the highway, and the muffler, engine and power mechanism of
every vehicle shall be so equipped and adjusted as to prevent the escape of
excessive fumes or smoke.
(Ord. 431, passed 9-13-1965) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.18 OPERATORS OF VEHICLES.
   No person shall operate any vehicle upon the public streets or highways of
the Town of Clayton who is not 13 years of age or older and duly licensed by
the State of New Mexico as required by NMSA §§ 66-5-2 and 66-5-18, as amended,
the provisions of the sections of the statute being herein incorporated by this
express reference.
(Ord. 431, passed 9-13-1965) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.19 OPERATION OF VEHICLES.
   (A)   No vehicle shall be operated with any person in front of the driver or
operator thereof, nor shall there be more than 2 persons on any vehicle.
   (B)   Not more than 2 vehicles shall be operated side by side in the same
lane of traffic on any multi-lane highway, nor upon any town street, highway or
alley, nor shall more than 1 lane at a time be occupied by 2 or more vehicles
abreast.
   (C)   Every vehicle shall observe all motor vehicle traffic regulations
provided by the laws of the State of New Mexico and ordinances of the Town of
Clayton, including but not limited to this subchapter.
   (D)   No vehicle shall occupy the left-hand or high speed lane of traffic in
any multi-lane highway so as to block use of same by overtaking motor vehicles,
but every vehicle shall when possible, move into the right-hand lane of any
multi-lane highway so as to yield the right-of-way to overtaking traffic; 2 or
more vehicles shall not travel abreast on any street or highway so as to
prevent other motor vehicles going in the same direction from overtaking or
passing them, but the vehicles shall move into a single- file position on any
street or highway, when reasonably required so to do by either an overtaking
vehicle going in the same direction attempting to pass or by an approaching
motor vehicle going in the opposite direction attempting to pass the vehicle or
vehicles.
(Ord. 431, passed 9-13-1965) Penalty, see §
72.99
§ 72.20 WHEN LIGHTS ARE REQUIRED.
   Any vehicle which shall be operated on any street or highway within the town
at any time within a ½ hour after sunset to a ½ hour before sunrise, or at any
other time when there is not sufficient light to render clearly discernible
persons and vehicles on the highway at a distance of 500 feet ahead, shall
display lighted lamps and illuminating devices as hereinbefore required,
subject to exceptions with respect to vehicles lawfully parked upon any street
or highway within the town.
(Ord. 431, passed 9-13-1965)
RECREATIONAL OFF-HIGHWAY VEHICLES AND ALL-TERRAIN VEHICLES
§ 72.30 OPERATION.
   (A)   NMSA § 66-3-1011 provides for operation of recreational off-highway
vehicles and all-terrain vehicles on paved streets within the Town of Clayton
if authorized by resolution or ordinance of the Town of Clayton; subject to the
following terms, conditions, and structures of this section such vehicles are
authorized to operate on certain paved streets within the Town of Clayton.
   (B)   All such vehicles and their operators must comply with each and every
provision of NMSA § 66-3-1011 and any violation of that statute is a violation
of this section.
   (C)   All such vehicles may be operated within the Town of Clayton only
during daylight hours which are defined as one-half hour prior to sunrise
through one-half hour after sunset.
   (D)   Such vehicles shall not be operated on:
      (1)   That portion of First Street (US64/87) from the intersection of
First Street and North First Avenue on the north to the intersection of First
Street and West Avenue on the south.
      (2)   That portion of Main Street and Monroe Street (US56) from the
intersection of Main Street and West Avenue on the east to the intersection of
Monroe Street and North Fifth Avenue on the west.
      (3)   Those streets immediately adjacent to any hospital, nursing home,
or public school within the Town of Clayton.
   (E)   Such vehicles may cross the portions of First Street, Main Street, and
Monroe Street on which such vehicles are prohibited by this section only in the
manner permitted by NMSA § 66-3-1011.
(Ord. 701, passed 4-11-2018)
§ 72.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to $
10.99.
   (B)   Any person violating the provisions of §
72.01 shall be fined not more than $25 for any violation.
(Ord. 504, passed 7-11-1977)
   (C)   Any person violating any of the provisions of §§
72.15 through
72.20 shall be deemed guilty of an ordinance violation and upon conviction
thereof, shall be fined in an amount not exceeding $200, or shall be imprisoned
in the town jail for a period not exceeding 90 days.
(Ord. 431, passed 9-13-1965)
   (D)   Any violation of §
72.30 shall be cited into the Municipal Court of the Town of Clayton and upon
conviction a violator may be shall fined in an amount not to exceed $500 and/or
imprisoned for not more than 90 days.
Ord. 701, passed 4-11-2018
CHAPTER 73: PARKING REGULATIONS
Section
General Provisions
   
73.01   Unauthorized vehicles within designated handicapped parking spaces
   
73.02   Method of parking vehicles within town
   
73.03   Exceptions to parking in Fire District of town
   
73.04   Parking zones in areas not zoned commercial; procedure
 
   
73.99   Penalty
Cross-reference:
   State legislation on parking, see
Ch. 70
GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 73.01 UNAUTHORIZED VEHICLES WITHIN DESIGNATED HANDICAPPED PARKING SPACES.
   (A)   Parking in handicapped space. It shall be unlawful for any person to
park an unauthorized vehicle in a designated handicapped parking space.
   (B)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context indicates or requires a different
meaning.
      AUTHORIZED VEHICLE. A passenger motor vehicle owned by a disabled person
and carrying special registration license plates issued pursuant to NMSA § 66-
3-16, or similar legislation, or any passenger motor vehicle operated by, or
for the benefit of, a disabled person.
      DESIGNATED HANDICAPPED PARKING SPACE. Any parking space for passenger
motor vehicles clearly marked as a handicap parking space.
      DISABLED PERSON. Any person who has suffered loss or the loss of use by 1
or both legs, from any cause. Any person deemed to be legally blind shall also
fit within the class of DISABLED PERSONS for the purpose of this section.
HANDICAPPED PERSONS is synonymous with DISABLED PERSONS for the purpose of this
section.
(Ord. 539, passed 5-23-1983) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.02 METHOD OF PARKING VEHICLES WITHIN TOWN.
   The method of parking vehicles within the Town of Clayton, New Mexico, shall
be as follows:
   (A)   On Front Street and on Main Street between Third Street and Eighth
Street, vehicles left standing or parked shall be parked in the direction in
which traffic is facing, parallel to the curb and with the right wheels within
1 foot of the curb.
   (B)   On the following named streets: Main Street, between Front and Third
Streets; Second Street, between Chestnut and Walnut Streets; Chestnut Street,
between Front and Second Streets; Walnut Street, between Front and Second
Streets; Maple Street, between Front and Second Streets, and between Eighth and
Ninth Streets in the town, vehicles shall be turned to the right and parked at
the curb at an angle of 30 degrees to the curb with the right front wheel
against the curb, or as marked.
   (C)   On all public streets in areas of the town zoned commercial where
parking is permitted, such parking may be either parallel or at an angle in
conformance with the way such street is striped from time to time by the
governmental entity that has jurisdiction over such street; in the event that a
street in a commercial zone is not striped for parking either angle or parallel
parking is permissible.
   (D)   On all other streets, not specified herein, vehicles shall be parked
at the curb, within 1 foot thereof, and shall be parked in the direction in
which traffic is facing, that is, parallel parking shall be employed. If there
shall be no curb, then parking shall be within approximately 1 foot of the
established curb line.
   (E)   No vehicle may remain parked in the same place within the Business
District longer than 24 hours consecutively.
   (F)   (1)   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation
whatsoever to leave any trailer or any other vehicle which is not capable of
being self-propelled, parked and detached from its means of propulsion on any
of the following streets:
         (a)   On Main Street and Monroe Street at any place within the town
limits;
         (b)   On First Street at any point between Peach Street and Spruce
Street;
         (c)   On Maple Street between Front Street and First Street; and
         (d)   On Chestnut and Walnut Streets between Front Street and Second
Street.
      (2)   Any person engaged in the business of selling second-hand cars or
trucks or farm equipment, both new and used, including but not limited to self-
propelled farm vehicles, shall keep all the second-hand cars or trucks, farm
equipment and self-propelled farm vehicles offered for sale on private property
and shall not permit any of the same to remain upon any public highway of the
Town of Clayton.
   (G)   It shall be unlawful to leave any wrecked or disabled self-propelled
vehicle for more than 5 hours on any of the aforementioned streets within the
territorial limits hereinbefore set forth.
   (H)   In the event any trailer or other vehicle which is not capable of
being self-propelled is so parked while detached from means of propulsion for
any time whatsoever, or any wrecked or disabled self- propelled vehicle is left
upon any of the streets within the territorial limits herein before set forth
for more than 5 hours, the Chief of Police or any other police officer may
order the trailer or vehicle impounded and stored at any public garage at the
expense of the owner of any trailer or vehicle, in addition to any fine or
imprisonment which may be imposed under §
73.99(C) hereof for violation of this subchapter.
(Ord. 304, passed 12-9-1946; Am. Ord. 312, passed 3-8-1948; Am. Ord. 318,
passed 7-26-1948; Am. Ord. 419, passed 12-9-1963; Am. Ord. 426, passed 8-10-
1964; Am. Ord. 437, passed 6-26-1967; Am. Ord. 681, passed 8-10-2011) Penalty,
see §
73.99
§ 73.03 EXCEPTIONS TO PARKING IN FIRE DISTRICT OF TOWN.
   It shall be unlawful to double park any motor vehicle within that portion of
the Business District of the Town of Clayton known as the Fire Zone, except as
follows:
   (A)   Passenger vehicles may not be double parked for any period;
   (B)   Light delivery trucks, so long as actually necessary, double park on
the side being delivered to, provided there is no regular parking space within
100 feet of the door to which delivery is being made;
   (C)   On Saturdays and holidays between 10:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m., no
deliveries shall be made from any truck or car, unless parked at the curb in a
regular parking space;
   (D)   All trucks parking within the Fire Zone limits of the town shall be
under the direction of the Police Department at all times and hours, and that
at any time an owner or driver is ordered or asked to move a truck by a police
officer of the town, the owner or driver shall comply at once. No truck shall
park in front of any premises occupied in whole or in part by a church
building; and
   (E)   No vehicle may park in any alley at any time except while actually
engaged in loading or unloading.
(Ord. 304, passed 12-9-1946; Am. Ord. 311, passed 2-23-1948) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.04 PARKING ZONES IN AREAS NOT ZONED COMMERCIAL; PROCEDURE.
   (A)   Establishment of parking zones in area not zoned commercial upon
petition of residents. Whenever the residents of portions of the Town of
Clayton not zoned commercial and constituting at least 75% of the total number
of residents of a neighborhood petition the Town Manager to establish a special
neighborhood parking zone having boundaries which are coextensive with the
neighborhood as defined in the petition, the Town Manager shall, after the
review set forth herein, establish such zone, modify the zone or deny the
petition and the Chief of Police shall implement the decision of the Town
Manager. A resident for purposes of this section is defined as a person over
the age of 18 years who has actually lived within the neighborhood for 90 days
or more. If the Town Manager's approval to establish the neighborhood parking
zone as requested by the petitioners includes additional conditions,
restrictions, or constitute a change to the zone proposed by the petitioners,
the petitioners may, by written consent of 75% of the residents affected, agree
to the additional conditions, restrictions or changes, in which case the zone
shall be established in accordance with the recommendations of the Town
Manager. Should 75% of the petitioners fail to accept the decision of the Town
Manager, or should the town Manager deny the petition, the petitioners may,
within 15 days of the decision, appeal the decision to the Town Council by
delivering written notice of the appeal to the Town Clerk.
   (B)   Contents of petition.  In order to request the establishment of a
neighborhood parking zone, the residents of a neighborhood shall present a
written petition to the Town Manager. The petition shall include a description
of the affected area constituting the neighborhood which must be a contiguous
area large enough to efficiently comprise a parking zone, a statement of the
need for a restricted neighborhood parking zone, a description of the proposed
terms and conditions of the zone, and shall designate a representative of the
petitioners to whom all future communications should be addressed. The petition
shall, as of the date of its submission to the Town Manager, have appended to
it a verified list of alt residents of the affected area. The petition shall be
signed by at least 75% of the residents within the affected area and shall
identify, by address, the property of each signatory. The signatures need not
be acknowledged. For the purposes of determining if the requisite number of
signatures have been obtained, each occupied dwelling, and each occupied
residential unit such as an apartment shall be considered as being entitled to
at a minimum of one signature and the petitioners shall certify that best
efforts have been made to contact all residents.
   (C)   Terms of neighborhood zones.  In seeking to establish a neighborhood
parking zone, the residents shall propose the periods when parking is to be
restricted, the means of identifying vehicles owned by residents who may park
on the street during restricted hours, the number of nonresident parking
permits, if any, which may. be issued to each resident, and the desired means
of identifying nonresident vehicles as having permits allowing them to park
within the zone.
   (D)   Review of petition.  In reviewing a petition for the establishment of
a neighborhood parking zone, the Town Manager shall make inquiry of the police
department to determine if sufficient evidence of the need to establish such a
zone exists, the impact of such zone on surrounding neighborhoods, and whether
the zone could reasonably be enforced. The road department shall determine
whether the area can be reasonably marked as having restricted parking and
whether the hours of the restrictions are reasonable. The Town Manager may
contact such other departments as may be deemed appropriate in order to seek
their opinions as to whether or not the zone should be created and if any
additional terms or conditions are advisable.
   (E)   Expenses of establishing zones. The Town Manager shall have the
discretion to determine whether or not the petitioners shall be required to
bear, the costs of establishing such a neighborhood parking zone. In the event
that such reimbursement is to be required, the Town Manager may consider the
cost of installation of all signage, and the cost of the means of identifying
vehicles as being permitted to park within the zone. The Town Manager may
require the petitioners to make satisfactory arrangements for such
reimbursement prior to the establishment of the zone and may require the
residents to pay a reasonable fee, not to exceed $3 per permit, to reimburse
the town for the actual costs of processing and issuing each vehicular permit.
Lost permits may be replaced only by payment of a fee not to exceed $10.
   (F)   Illegal parking within zones. It shall be a violation of this division
to park on the street in a neighborhood parking zone without displaying the
appropriate temporary or permanent permit to park therein. It shall be an
affirmative defense to the violation of this division that the vehicle is owned
by a resident of the neighborhood and that a permit has been obtained for that
vehicle within 5 days of that date of violation.
   (G)   Establishment of zone upon petition by town.  In the event that any
department or division of the town deems it advisable to establish a
neighborhood parking zone without the initiation of a petition by (he residents
of the affected area, a petition may be filed with Town Manager. The petition
shall contain all of the information required by division (A) with the
exception of the requirement of the residents' signature.
   (H)   Administration. The administration of all neighborhood parking zones
shall be the responsibility of the Town Manager or the Manager's designee. As
used herein, the term ADMINISTRATION includes the issuance and revocation of
permits, the establishment and dissolution of neighborhood parking zones, and
the installation of appropriate signs. The Chief of Police or the Chief’s
designee is responsible for the enforcement of the regulations within each
zone.
   (I)   Modification or dissolution of zone. A neighborhood parking zone may
be modified or dissolved upon petition of the residents or upon petition of the
town. In either event, the procedures set forth in this division shall apply.
   (J)   Power Retained by Board of Trustees.  Nothing in this chapter shall
restrict the power of the Board of Trustees to regulate parking within the Town
of Clayton on or by any other lawful means.
(Ord. 684, passed 9-14-2011) Penalty, see §
73.99
§ 73.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person who violates any provision of this chapter for which no
penalty is provided shall be subject to the terms of §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person found guilty of violating the provisions of §
73.01 shall be punished by a fine of $10.
   (C)   The penalties established for violations of §
73.04 are as follows:
      (1)   For a first offense, a fine of $50.
      (2)   For a second offense within a 12-month period, a fine of $250.
      (3)   For a third and subsequent offense within a 12-month period, a fine
of $500.
      (4)   The Municipal Court shall have the authority to suspend the fine on
the first offense but may not defer the conviction.
      (5)   In the event of a third or subsequent offense within a 12 month
period, the vehicle shall be towed or immobilized. The vehicle shall not be
released until the Municipal Court has provided clearance stating that all
outstanding fines and fees, including the cost of immobilizing or towing the
vehicle, have been paid. An immobilized vehicle may be subsequently be removed
from the neighborhood.
      (6)   For the purposes of this section, violations of the neighborhood
parking zone shall be charged lo the vehicle owner and not to the driver.
      (7)   The fines established herein are exclusive of any mandatory fees
which are required to be collected by the Municipal Court.
(Ord. 539, passed 5-23-1983; Am. Ord. 684, passed 9-14-2011)

SCHEDULE II: STREET CROSSINGS.
   A street crossing shall be created across the right-of-way of the railway by
extending certain streets as hereinafter set forth.
   (A)   Monroe Street shall be extended for the purpose by extending the
northerly line of the Monroe Street across the right-of-way of the railway to
the westerly boundary of Front Street; thence, following the line of Front
Street along the line of the right-of-way of the railway in a southerly
direction for a distance of 54 feet to a point on the line; thence westerly
parallel with the northerly line of Monroe Street, as extended to a point on
the easterly line of Railway Avenue.
   (B)   Main Street shall be extended for the purpose of creating a crossing
of the right-of-way of the railway by extending the northerly and southerly
boundaries across the right-of-way to the easterly line of Railway Avenue.
   (C)   Pine Street shall be extended for the purpose of creating a crossing
of the right-of-way of the railway by extending the northerly and southerly
boundaries across the right-of-way to the easterly line of Railway Avenue.
   (D)   Broadway Street shall be extended for the purpose of creating a
crossing of the right-of-way of the railway by extending the northerly and
southerly boundaries across the right-of-way to the easterly line of Railway
Avenue.
   (E)   Magnolia Street shall be extended for the purpose of creating a
crossing of the right-of-way of the railway by extending the northerly and
southerly boundaries across the right-of-way to the easterly boundary or line
of Railway Avenue.
(Ord. 141, passed 6-8-1925)

above required shall be made not more than 25 feet back of the street

cross or enter upon the intersection of Court Street and First Avenue, shall
bring the vehicle to a complete stop.

Street from either Front Street, Second Street, Third Street, Fourth Street,
Fifth Street, Sixth Street or Seventh Street shall bring the vehicle to a
complete stop before crossing or entering upon Main Street.
      (2)   The driver of any vehicle intending to cross or enter upon First
Street shall bring the vehicle to a complete stop before crossing or entering
upon First Street.
      (3)   The driver of any vehicle intending to cross or enter upon Monroe
Street or into the curves of the cutoff of Monroe Street, shall bring the
vehicle to a complete stop before crossing or entering upon Monroe Street.
(Ord. 304, passed 12-9-1946)

§ 90.01 PUBLIC STREETS AND ALLEYS USED FOR SALES OF VEHICLES BY BUSINESSES;
PROHIBITED.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation who or which
is engaged in the business of selling, trading, bartering or exchanging new or
used motor vehicles to park or permit the parking of the vehicles, new, used or
held for sale upon the public streets of the Town of Clayton.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to park or
leave any motor vehicle which is not in operating condition upon the public
streets of the town for a period of time of more than 24 hours.
   (C)   Any police officer of the town who finds any motor vehicle on the
public streets of the town in violation of this section shall obtain wrecker
service and have the vehicle removed from the street, and the owner of the
motor vehicle shall be liable for the reasonable cost of removing and storing
the vehicle or vehicles.
   (D)   As used in this section, the term MOTOR VEHICLE shall mean every
vehicle which is self-propelled or was originally manufactured to be self-
propelled.

§ 90.02 SWIMMING IN CLAYTON POOL AT CERTAIN HOURS PROHIBITED.
   (A)   The Board of Trustees from time to time, and without the adoption of a
new ordinance on the subject, may determine the hours of swimming at the
Clayton Municipal Swimming Pool, and when the hours of swimming are posted in a
prominent place at the pool, it shall be unlawful to go swimming at the pool
other than during the hours so posted.
   (B)   It shall likewise be unlawful, except during the hours when the pool
is officially open, to in any manner enter the enclosure surrounding the pool
whether for the purpose of swimming or any other purpose without having been
duly authorized so to do.

electric light, telephone or telegraph pole located on any street or alley
within the town, or to run any radio aerial or wire over or under any power,
electric light, telephone or telegraph line located in any street or alley
within the town, or to nail, screw, bolt or in any manner attach to any light,
power, telephone or telegraph pole within the town any bill, poster, sign or
any foreign attachment whatsoever.
(Ord. 187, passed 6-24-1929)

CHAPTER 91: FIRE PREVENTION; FIREWORKS
Section
Fireworks
   
91.01   Prohibiting the sale of certain fireworks
Fire Limits
   
91.20   Fire limits of the town
 
   
91.99   Penalty
FIREWORKS
§ 91.01 PROHIBITING THE SALE OF CERTAIN FIREWORKS.
   (A)   Prohibition. The sale or use of those fireworks defined in the New
Mexico Fireworks Licensing and Safety Act being NMSA §§ 60-2C-1 et seq., as
“aerial devices” and “ground audible devices” within the town is prohibited
subject only to those exceptions in division (B) below; provided, however, that
the prohibition on use of the devices shall not apply to public displays by the
Town of Clayton’s Fire Department.
   (B)   Exceptions.
      (1)   Sale. Aerial devices and ground audible devices may be sold within
the town only:
         (a)   During the period between June 20 and July 6 of each year and
between the hours of 9:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m.;
         (b)   By a vendor who has a valid license or permit issued under the
New Mexico Fireworks Licensing and Safety Act by the State Fire Marshal’s
office;
         (c)   By a vendor who has a valid business license appropriate for the
vendor’s type of business issued by the town;
         (d)   By a vendor who has a valid fireworks sales permit which allows
for the sale of aerial devices and ground audible devices issued by the town;
         (e)   At a location consistent with the State Fire Marshal’s permit,
approved in writing by the Fire Chief of the town in exercise of Fire Chief’s
discretion considering fire prevention and safety factors, including without
limitation, current conditions of weather, precipitation and dryness; and
         (f)   To persons of the age of 18 years and older.
      (2)   Aerial devices. Use of aerial devices and ground audible devices
may be used within the town only:
         (a)   During the period between June 20 and July 6 of each year and
between the hours of 9:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m.;
         (b)   On private property; for purposes of this section PRIVATE
PROPERTY does not include any property owned by the Town of Clayton, the County
of Union, the Clayton Public Schools or the State of New Mexico, nor does it
include any public street, highway, alley, park, fair grounds or recreational
facility;
         (c)   With the consent of the owners, occupiers and proprietors of the
property on which the devices are being ignited and of all property on which
the devices may land and of all property from which the devices are audible;
and
         (d)   By persons of the age of 18 years or older or by persons under
the age of 18 years who are under the direct supervision and in the continuous
presence of a person of the age of 18 years or older.
   (C)   Permits. No person shall sell fireworks within the town, without first
having obtained a permit from the Town Clerk-Treasurer of the Town of Clayton
the fee for the permits shall be $50 each without proration and the permits
shall be issued for period of 1 year beginning February 1, and ending January
31. There shall be 2 types of permits issued:
      (1)   Permits for sale of fireworks other than aerial devices and ground
audible devices. Permits may be issued for the sale of fireworks other than
aerial devices and ground audible devices; and the Town Clerk-Treasurer may
issue without limitation as many permits for sale of fireworks other than
aerial devices and ground audible devices as there may be a demand for the
permits; and
      (2)   Permits for sale of fireworks including aerial devices and ground
audible devices. Permits may be issued for the sale of fireworks including
aerial devices and ground audible devices; provided, however, that the Town
Clerk-Treasurer shall issue no more than 3 permits during any 1 permit year
which permits shall be issued without preference on a first-come, first-served
basis.
(Ord. 593, passed 9-12-1994) Penalty, see §
91.99
Cross-reference:
   Possession of fireworks, public displays, see §
132.63
