GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 95.01 PROHIBITING BREAKING, DESTROYING OR BREAKING DOWN GLOBES OF STREET
LIGHTS.
   Any person who shall deface, injure, destroy, break down or in any manner
damage any globe or standard of any of the street lighting system of the town,
or any part of either, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon
conviction thereof shall be fined as set forth in §
95.99.
(Ord. 195, passed 2-10-1930) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.02 SKATING UPON STREETS AND SIDEWALKS.
   Any person who shall skate upon or across any sidewalks or street crossing
or who shall engage in any sport or play upon the sidewalk or street crossing
within the Business District of the town shall be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor, and shall, for every offense, be punished by a fine as set forth
in §
95.99.
(Ord. 61, passed 6-5-1912) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.03 ENCROACHMENT AND OBSTRUCTIONS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person, persons, firm, co-partnership or
corporation, to place, hang or swing, upon or over any sidewalk in the town,
any awning, sign, sign-board, plank, rod or other attachment, device or
structure, unless the same or all parts thereof shall be 6-1/2 feet above the
surface of the sidewalk.
   (B)   Any and all awnings, signs, sign-boards or other attachment, device or
structure or any portion thereof, now hanging or constructed, which shall, at
any time, be nearer than 6-1/2 feet from the surface of the sidewalk, are
hereby declared obstructions of the sidewalk, and shall be immediately removed
or raised upon notice from the Town Marshal.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful for any person, persons, firm, co-partnership or
corporation to place, stack or pile upon the sidewalks or streets in the town,
any boxes, barrels, groceries, dry goods, hay, grain, implements, machinery or
any other things which constitute obstructions to the sidewalks or streets, and
the sidewalks and streets shall at all times be kept free from obstructions of
every kind; provided, however, that nothing herein shall be so construed as to
prohibit merchants or other business persons, firms, co-partnerships or
corporations from temporarily using the sidewalks or streets in loading or
unloading merchandise.
(Ord. 24, passed 6-30-1908) Penalty, see §
95.99
PAVING OF STREETS; MAINTENANCE AND REPAIR
§ 95.20 PROTECT STREETS AND HIGHWAYS FROM DAMAGE; MOVING BUILDINGS AND DEBRIS.
   (A)   Any tractor or other vehicle having lugs is not permitted to operate
on the streets and highways of the town without a special permit in writing
first had and obtained from either the Mayor or the Police Department of the
town; the permit shall not be granted if it appears the operation of any
vehicle will result in damage to the streets and highways of the town, in the
discretion of the licensing authority.
   (B)   Trees or any portion thereof, dead livestock or any other material or
object, of whatsoever nature, shall not be dragged upon the streets and
highways of the town, without a special permit in writing first had and
obtained from either the Mayor or the Police Department; the permit shall not
be granted if it appears that the dragging would result in the littering with
debris of any streets and highways of the town to any considerable extent, in
the discretion of the licensing authority.
   (C)   Any person, firm or corporation obtaining any permit in writing as set
forth in division (B) above shall clean up all litter, mess and debris left by
any dragging so done and shall constitute a separate violation of this section.
   (D)   Any person, firm or corporation intending to bring any building
through or upon the streets and highways of the town shall first obtain a
permit in writing so to do from the Mayor or the Police Department, and at the
same time shall pay in advance a license fee of $15 an hour to the Town Clerk-
Treasurer for the time estimated to complete the moving of the building either
to its intended location within the town, or through the town; the estimate to
be made by the Mayor or the Police Department, with a minimum license fee of
$15; and in addition, the person, firm or corporation shall deposit in advance
of any moving, with the Town Clerk-Treasurer, the cost estimated for moving and
repairing any poles or wires, as determined in the discretion of the Mayor or
the Police Department, and shall reimburse the town for any actual cost in
addition thereto, occasioned by the moving when completed; any surplus above
actual cost of moving poles or wires shall be refunded to the person making the
deposit with the Town Clerk-Treasurer, but the license fee shall be retained by
the town, at the rate of $15 for each hour or part thereof consumed.
(Ord. 436, passed 3-27-1967) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.21 PROCEDURE OF PAVING AND IMPROVING CERTAIN STREETS; ASSESSMENTS.
   (A)   All the proceedings heretofore had, taken, done or performed in
connection with paving and improving the streets specified in the plans and
plats, and to be of benefit to the property described in the modified
assessment roll on file in the Town Clerk-Treasurer’s office, be and the same
are in all respects hereby ratified, approved and confirmed.
   (B)   For the purpose of paying the cost and expenses of the improvements,
except the sum of $20,000 per year, during the time that the improvements are
under construction which shall be paid from the Treasury of the town, there be
and there hereby is levied and assessed against the lots, tracts and parcels of
lands set out in the assessment roll as modified and confirmed, which is on
file in the Town Clerk-Treasurer’s office in the Town of Clayton, New Mexico,
and in the amounts as set out in the assessment roll, as modified and
confirmed, opposite each lot, parcel or tract land.
   (C)   The assessments shall be due and payable at the office of the Town
Clerk-Treasurer as follows:
      (1)   The sum of $0.25 per annum per front foot for each foot fronting
upon the streets to be improved, the first payment being due and payable at the
office of the Town Treasury on January 25, 1958, and a like installment due on
January 25 of each year thereafter until the time as paving is laid down in
front of a particular lot, tract or parcel of land, at which time the $0.25 per
front foot charge per annum payment shall cease upon the particular lot, tract
or parcel of land in front of which paving has been laid down and the balance
of the assessment as set forth in the assessment roll, as modified, shall be
paid as set out in division (C)(2) below hereof.
      (2)   After deducting from the assessment upon each particular lot, tract
or parcel of land in front of which paving has been laid down, the amount paid
under division (C)(1) above, that is, at the rate of $0.25 per front foot per
annum, the balance of the assessment as shown on the assessment roll, as
modified, shall be due and payable at the office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer on
the first day of January of the year immediately following the time that the
paving is laid down in front of each particular lot, tract or parcel of land
without demand by the town, provided that all the assessments made at the
election of the owner be paid in installments without interest. Failure to pay
the whole assessment when due as provided herein shall be conclusively
considered and held and election to pay in installments, as herein after
provided. In case of an election to pay in installments, the assessments shall
be payable at the office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer in 10 equal annual
installments, the first of which installment shall be due and payable on or
before January 1 of the year immediately following the laying down of pavement
in front of the lots, tracts and parcels of land within the year, and the
remainder of the assessment shall be due and payable successively on the first
day of year thereafter until paid in full, and provided further that the
installments may, at the election of the owner, be paid monthly commencing on
January 1 of the year immediately following the year in which the pavement is
laid down in front of the owner’s property. Failure to pay any installments
provided in division (C)(1) above or this section, when due, shall at the
election of the town cause the whole of the unpaid principal to become due and
payable immediately. Delinquent installments shall bear interest at the rate of
8% per annum from date of delinquency.
   (D)   The amounts assessed as aforesaid shall be a lien upon the lots and
parcels of land from the time this section becomes effective, which lien shall
be superior to all liens, except the lien for general taxes, but the sale of
any lot or parcel of land for general taxes shall not relieve the lot or parcel
of land from the assessments or the lien thereof. It shall be the duty of the
Town Clerk-Treasurer within 60 days hereafter to make out, sign, attest with
the seal of the town, and file for record in the office of the County Clerk of
Union County, New Mexico, a claim of lien for the amount due and assessed
against each lot or parcel of land as specified in the assessment roll, as
modified, and all purchasers, mortgagees and encumbrances of the lots and
parcels of land shall take the same subject to the lien. In case any lot or
parcel of land so assessed becomes delinquent in the payment of the assessment
or any installment thereof, the Board of Trustees shall cause the lien to be
enforced and foreclosed as provided by law.
When the assessments and the installments thereof have been paid in full, it
shall be the duty of the Town Clerk-Treasurer to release and discharge the lien
and liability.
   (E)   Any owner who wishes to do so may pay all of the assessment against
his or her property in advance, and in case of full payment in advance shall be
allowed a discount of 2% upon the total assessment.
(Ord. 379, passed 12-9-1957)
§ 95.22 ESTABLISHING STREET IMPROVEMENTS.
   (A)   (1)   Whenever the Board of Trustees shall receive a petition in
writing, executed by the owners of more than ½ of the front feet of property
abutting upon any highway or portion thereof proposed to be improved,
requesting it to order the improvements of the highway or part thereof therein
described, the Board of Trustees shall pass a resolution ordering the
improvement made in conformity with the petition and the passage of the
resolution shall be conclusive of the public necessity therefor. The resolution
shall in general terms set forth the nature and extent of the improvements to
be made, the section or sections of any public highway or highways to be
improved and the materials or material with which the improvements are to be
constructed and the manner in which the cost thereof is to be discharged. The
resolution may specify alternative materials of which the improvements may be
constructed, at the option of the Board of Trustees, and different and
alternative plans and methods of construction and paying for same unless the
petitioners have specified in their original petition a particular kind of
paving or improvements, in which event the Board of Trustees shall be limited
to the kind of improvement so specified.
      (2)   Upon the passage of the resolutions, it shall be the duty of the
Town Engineer, or an engineer as may be designated by the Board of Trustees, to
forthwith prepare specifications for the construction specified in the
resolution. The specifications shall be submitted to and approved by the Board
of Trustees. When the specifications have been approved, it shall be the duty
of the Town Clerk- Treasurer, or the officer as may be designated by the Board
of Trustees, to at once advertise for sealed bids for the performing of the
work in accordance with the specifications. The advertisement shall be
published in some newspaper of general circulation in the town not less than 10
days prior to the date mentioned therein for the opening of bids. The Board of
Trustees shall have the right to accept the most advantageous bid or bids to
the town and owners of property abutting the proposed improvements. No bid
shall be amended or changed after being opened by the Board of Trustees.
   (B)   When the bid or bids shall have been accepted, the town shall enter
into a written contract with the successful bidder or bidders for the
performance of the work, which shall be executed by the Mayor, or the other
officer as may be designated by the Board of Trustees, and attested with the
corporate seal by the Town Clerk-Treasurer, or other officer as may be
designated by the Board of Trustees. The bidder or bidders may be required to
enter into bond for the performance of the work, or maintenance and repair
thereof, for the period of time as may be determined by the Board of Trustees
from completion, in case the materials, methods or plans of construction
employed therein shall prove defective.
   (C)   The contract and bond, if any, having been approved by the Board of
Trustees shall be the duty of the Town Engineer, or engineer as may be
designated by the Board of Trustees, to prepare and file with the Board of
Trustees a statement containing the name of the person, firm, corporation or
estate owning the property abutting on the proposed improvements and describing
each parcel by lot or block number, number of front feet or otherwise, so as to
sufficiently identify the same. The statement shall contain the estimated cost
and expense of the improvement; the boundaries of the assessment district, if
any, to be formed, the route of the improvement by streets, alleys or
otherwise, the place of commencement and ending of the proposed improvements, a
description of the property to be affected belonging to the owners to be served
and the amount of the assessment against the property with a statement of set-
offs, if any. The Board of Trustees shall examine the statement and after
correcting any errors therein, approve the same, but no error, mistake or
omission shall invalidate the same or any assessment made thereunder. After
approving the statement, if it is fully determined to assess a part or all of
the costs of the improvement against property owners and their property, the
Board of Trustees shall so declare by resolution, ordering a hearing to be
given to owners of the abutting property and notice thereof, and the notice
shall be given and the hearing held in compliance with the provisions of the
Act of the Second Session of the First Legislature approved on March 11, 1913
set out above.
   (D)   After the hearing has been closed, the Board of Trustees shall from
the evidence before it, determine the amounts, if any, to be assessed against
each owner and his or her property, and shall by ordinance, assess the same
against the property of each owner and declare the amount so assessed to be a
personal liability of its owner as provided by the act of the legislature. The
total amount to be assessed against the owners and their property shall be
proportioned among them in accordance with the front feet plan or rule, in
proportion as the frontage of each owner is to the whole frontage to be
improved; provided that if the application of this rule shall, in the opinion
of the Board of Trustees, be unjust or unequal, or result in individual cases,
in an assessment in excess of special benefits received from the improvements,
then the Board of Trustees shall adopt the rule of apportionment as shall
effect a substantial equality and uniformity between the owners, considering
benefits received by and burdens imposed upon them are their property.
(Ord. 68, passed 1- -1914)
CURBS, GUTTERS AND SIDEWALKS; MAINTENANCE AND CONSTRUCTION
§ 95.35 SIDEWALK, CURB AND GUTTER IMPROVEMENTS IN BUSINESS DISTRICT;
MAINTENANCE.
   (A)   This section concerns and affects the Business District of the town
which is defined as that area:
      (1)   Bounded on the north by East Broadway Street and including the
properties on both sides of the street which abut East Broadway Street;
      (2)   Bounded on the east by Third Street and including the properties on
both sides of the street which abut Third Street;
      (3)   Bounded on the south by Maple Street and including the properties
on both sides of the street which abut on Maple Street; and
      (4)   Bounded on the west by the railroad tracks.
   (B)   All owners of property which abut the streets within the Business
District shall construct and maintain sidewalks, curbs and gutters or shall
renovate existing sidewalks, curbs and gutters in accordance with the
specifications on file at the Town Office; all the construction and maintenance
or renovation shall be completed within 2 years of the effective date of this
section, which date is referred to as the “completion date”.
   (C)   After the completion date, all sidewalks, curbs and gutters shall be
repaired and maintained and no property owner shall permit any crack, chip,
break or other failure of any part of that property owner’s sidewalk, curb or
gutter as follows:
      (1)   Vertical separations of 3/4 inch or more;
      (2)   Horizontal separations of 3/4 inch or more;
      (3)   Holes or depressions of 3 inches or more in diameter and 3/4 inch
or more in depth;
      (4)   Spalling over 50% of a single 6-foot by 6-foot square or panel of
the sidewalk with 1 or more depressions of 3/4 inch or more;
      (5)   A single square or panel of sidewalk, curb or gutter, cracked in
such a manner that no part thereof has a piece greater than 1 square foot or is
cracked in such a manner that it constitutes a danger or a potential danger to
the public;
      (6)   A sidewalk, curb or gutter with any part thereof missing 3/4 inch
or more; and
      (7)   A deviation on the staked and constructed grade of 3/4 inch or more
as to any sidewalk, curb or gutter newly constructed.
   (D)   No person shall remove, deface, damage, destroy or otherwise alter the
condition of any sidewalk, curb or gutter except when making immediate repairs.
Any damage or destruction, which is occasioned by any party whether it be
accidental or otherwise, shall be repaired or replaced immediately by the
property owner at the property owner’s expense. If the damage or destruction
was occasioned by the actions of a person other than the property owner, the
abutting property owner shall have the right to recover the cost of repair or
replacement from the responsible person according to applicable law and
available remedies, but the actions of the third person shall not alleviate the
abutting property owner of the responsibility to maintain, replace or repair
damaged, destroyed or defective sidewalks.
(Ord. 645, passed 11-15-2005) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.36 NO CONSTRUCTION WITHOUT A PERMIT.
   No sidewalks, curbs and gutters shall be built within the limits of the
town, without obtaining permits to do so from the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
(Ord. 404, passed 8-14-1961; Am. Ord. 536, passed 8-23-1982) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.37 FEE TO BE PAID.
   All companies, firms, corporations or individuals, before beginning on
construction work, shall pay a fee to the Town Clerk-Treasurer of $2.50 for the
first 50 feet of curb and gutter front footage and $1.00 for each additional 50
feet contiguous thereto, and the companies, firms, corporations or individuals
shall obtain and pay for the services of a licensed professional engineer or
licensed surveyor to furnish line and grade stakes according to which the
sidewalk and curb shall be built.
(Ord. 404, passed 8-14-1961; Am. Ord. 536, passed 8-23-1982)
§ 95.38 PERMIT NEEDED AND WORK STAKED OUT.
    No sidewalk or curb shall be built before a permit has been obtained and
the work properly staked out.
(Ord. 404, passed 8-14-1961; Am. Ord. 536, passed 8-23-1982) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.39 BUILD AT GRADES ESTABLISHED.
   All sidewalks, curbs and gutters shall be built at the grades established by
the Engineer.
(Ord. 404, passed 8-14-1961; Am. Ord. 536, passed 8-23-1982)
§ 95.40 BUILT IN SPECIFIC WAYS.
   All sidewalks, except in the Business District, shall be built in 1 of 3
ways:
   (A)   According to the standard section on file in the Town Office, i.e.,
the sidewalk shall be placed 2 feet from the property line, and 4 feet wide
extending toward the street. All curbs shall be 10 feet from the property line,
in the 80 foot streets and 20 feet from the property line, in the 100-foot
streets, leaving 60 feet of clear roadway in both cases.
   (B)   In the event a majority of the owners on 1 side of any street, avenue
or highway in any block in the town agree in writing that their sidewalk should
be immediately adjacent and against the curb of the street, avenue or highway,
the writing shall be filed with the Town Clerk-Treasurer, whereupon they shall
be entitled to construct a sidewalk 3-1/2 feet wide and 4 inches thick
immediately adjacent to and against the curb line on the side of the street
adjacent to their properties; provided, that if any sidewalk shall already
exist along any part of the block on the same side of the street as the lots of
the consenting property owner, they must obtain permission in writing from the
owners of the lots adjacent to the sidewalks already in place, to destroy the
same and construct a new sidewalk adjoining the curb line; if the permission
cannot be obtained, then no sidewalk on the street, avenue or highway may be
constructed next to the curb along the front lines of the lots fronting upon
the street, avenue or highway, but any sidewalk shall then be constructed only
in line with the existing sidewalk already in place, unless the existing
sidewalk shall be in such poor condition that same shall be condemned by the
Town Engineer as hereinafter provided; likewise, if a sidewalk exists next to
the curb in part of any block, the remainder of the sidewalk on same street in
the block must be constructed next to the curb.
   (C)   In the event any property owner desires to construct a sidewalk next
to the curb line along the side line of his or her lot, where he or she owns up
to the alley the entire lot whose side line is immediately adjacent to the
street, avenue or highway, in the town, he or she may at his or her option
construct a sidewalk either as provided in division (A) above, or the sidewalk
3-1/2 feet wide and 4 inches thick adjacent to and against the curb line of the
street, avenue or highway; provided that no sidewalk next to the curb shall be
constructed as provided in division (B) above or this division, unless the curb
and gutter have already been constructed or are constructed at or about the
same time as any sidewalk immediately adjacent to the curb.
(Ord. 404, passed 8-14-1961)
§ 95.41 CONSTRUCTED AS 1 UNIT.
   All curbs and gutters shall be constructed together as 1 unit, with the curb
7-1/2 inches high above the gutter, and the gutter shall be 24 inches wide, and
the curb and gutter shall be otherwise constructed as prescribed by the Town
Engineer.
(Ord. 404, passed 8-14-1961)
§ 95.42 BUILT OF CONCRETE; PROPORTIONS.
   (A)   All sidewalks and curbs shall be built of concrete mixed in the
following proportions; 1 part approved cement, 2 parts clean sand and 3 parts
crushed salpais rock or gravel, and shall be given a float finish on top.
   (B)   Sidewalks shall be blocked in 4-foot squares and otherwise in
accordance with specifications by the Town Engineer.
(Ord. 404, passed 8-14-1961)
§ 95.43 INSPECTION AND APPROVAL.
   All sidewalks and curbs shall be subject to the inspection and approval of
the Town Engineer.
(Ord. 404, passed 8-14-1961)
§ 95.44 REMOVING MATERIALS.
   All materials or workmanship condemned by the Town Engineer shall be removed
at once; in the event the Town Engineer upon inspection of any old sidewalk
shall find the same to be so broken, cracked or uneven that in his or her
discretion he or she shall deem the same to be unsafe for public travel, he or
she shall give notification to the adjoining property owner in writing of the
condemnation and the property owner shall have 10 days after receipt of the
notification to remove the defective work; or, if in the judgment of the Town
Engineer, the sidewalk shall be capable of repair so as to render the same
reasonably safe for public travel, he or she shall so notify the adjoining
property owner who shall have 10 days after the notification in writing to
repair or to cause the same to be properly repaired, subject to the approval of
the Town Engineer of the workmanship and materials used when same is completed.
(Ord. 404, passed 8-14-1961)
§ 95.45 REPAIR AND REPLACEMENT.
   In the event any adjoining property owner fails to replace or repair, as the
case may be, any new or previously existing sidewalk condemned by the Town
Engineer, the Board of Trustees of the town may, upon the filing of the report
of the Engineer, take further action as is by statute provided, concerning the
replacement or repair of the sidewalk.
(Ord. 404, passed 8-14-1961)
§ 95.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person who shall violate the provisions of §
95.01 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall
be fined in any sum not exceeding $200 or imprisoned in the town or county jail
for any period not exceeding 90 days, or punished by both the fine and
imprisonment in the discretion of the court trying the case.
(Ord. 195, passed 2-10-1930)
   (C)   Any person who shall violate the provisions of §
95.02 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and shall, for every offense, be
punished by a fine of not less than $3 nor more than $10, or by imprisonment in
the town jail for not less than 3 nor more than 10 days, or by both the fine
and imprisonment in the discretion of the court.
(Ord. 61, passed 6-5-1912)
   (C)   Any person who shall violate any of the foregoing sections of §
95.03 shall, upon conviction, be punished by a fine of not less than $5 nor
more than $25, or by imprisonment in the town or county jail for a period of
not less than 5 days nor more than 30 days, or by both the fine and
imprisonment in the discretion of the court trying the case, and each day that
any obstructions hereby prohibited are allowed to remain upon or over the
sidewalks or streets, in violation of §
95.03, shall constitute a separate and distinct offense and shall be subject to
the penalties hereof.
(Ord. 24, passed 6-30-1908)
   (D)   (1)   Violation of any section of §
95.20 shall constitute a separate and distinct offense from violation of any
other section thereof.
      (2)   Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the provisions of
§
95.20 shall be punished for each offense by a fine not to exceed $300, or by
imprisonment not to exceed 90 days, in the discretion of the court.
(Ord. 436, passed 3-27-1967)
   (E)   Any person violating §
95.35 shall be subject to citation into Municipal Court and upon conviction
shall be fined up to $500 or imprisoned up to 90 days or both the fine and
imprisonment. Each day that a violation exists constitutes a separate offense.
(Ord. 645, passed 11-15-2005)
   (F)   Any person, company, firm or corporation who shall violate any of the
provisions of §§
95.36 through 95.45 or any section, clause or paragraph or any section of this
subchapter, or who shall assist in any violation, shall for each and every
violation be deemed guilty of violating §§
95.36 through
95.45 and upon conviction thereof, be fined in any sum not less than $10 nor
more than $100.
(Ord. 404, passed 8-14-1961)

§ 96.01 JUNK ON VACANT LOTS.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context indicates or requires a different
meaning.
      JUNK. Any worn out, discarded or abandoned materials, including but not
by way of limitation refuse, rubbish, old rags, metals, rubber, glass parts of
machines and vehicles, waste paper, cloth, textiles and old lumber having only
salvage value.
      VACANT LOT. Any lot which is not being used for dwelling or business
purposes and which is not being used as a JUNK YARD as is authorized under §
94.01.
   (B)   Clean lots. It shall be the duty of all persons, partnerships or
corporations, who own vacant lots within the corporate limits of the Town of
Clayton, New Mexico, to keep the vacant lots free and clear of all junk.
   (C)   Junk on lots.
      (1)   It shall be the duty of the Town Clerk-Treasurer of the Town of
Clayton, New Mexico, whenever it shall come to his or her attention that there
is junk on a vacant lot within the corporate limits of the town, to notify the
owner of the lot, asking him or her to remove the junk.
      (2)   If, within 10 days of the notification, the owner has not complied
with the notice, the Town of Clayton, New Mexico shall clear the lot of the
junk.
      (3)   Charges for the clearing of the lot and the removal of the junk by
the town shall constitute liens upon the property so cleared, and shall be
filed for record in office of the County Clerk of Union County, New Mexico. The
liens shall be superior to all other liens, except general property taxes and
may be foreclosed in the manner provided for by law for the foreclosure of
municipal assessment liens.
(Ord. 383, passed 6-23-1958)
§ 96.02 PIT OR OUTDOOR TOILETS.
   (A)   Outdoor and pit toilets, not connected with the sanitary sewer system
of the town, nor to any private cesspool or septic tank, are hereby declared a
nuisance and a menace to the public health and welfare.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for the owner, tenant or other person in charge
of any premises within the town to maintain, construct or use thereon any
outdoor or pit toilet not connected either with the sanitary sewer system of
the town or else with a private cesspool or septic tank of approved type of
construction.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful to construct a private cesspool or septic tank at
any place within the sanitary sewer district of the town or upon any premises
outside the sanitary sewer district which reasonably has access to the sanitary
sewer system of the town.
(Ord. 334, passed 9-12-1949) Penalty, see §
96.99
Cross-reference:
   Requirement to connect to sanitary sewer system, see §
52.001
§ 96.03 LOW TREE BRANCHES A NUISANCE.
   (A)   It is declared a nuisance and unlawful for the owner or occupant of
any premises within the town to permit the growth of branches or trees upon the
parking in front of the premises in the way that same overhang the sidewalks
with less than 7 feet of clearance between the sidewalk and overhanging limbs.
   (B)   It is declared a nuisance and unlawful for the owner or occupant of
any premises within the town to permit the growth or branches of trees upon the
parking in front of the premises in such a way that same shall project beyond
the curb line and into the public street, except and unless the branches or
tree limbs overhanging the public streets shall have a clearance of not less
than 10 feet between the established gutter level and any overhanging branches.
(Ord. 292, passed 3-14-1944) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.04 UNNECESSARY AND IMPROPER NOISES.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person or persons to make, assist in
making or allow or cause to be made unnecessary or improper noise or
disturbance within the Town of Clayton, New Mexico.
   (B)   UNNECESSARY OR IMPROPER NOISE OR DISTURBANCE is defined to mean and
include:
      (1)   The use and operation of any phonograph, radio or combination of
the same so that the sound there from is projected immediately into the street
by means of a street speaker. STREET shall be deemed to include sidewalk, and
this section shall be construed so as to prohibit what is commonly called a
“street speaker”, by whatsoever name known, by which sounds therefrom are
projected immediately into the street, and shall also be deemed to include any
radio or phonograph or combination of the 2 or the reproducing unit thereof
when so placed in any doorway or opening of any building or business
establishment within the Business District of the town so that the sound
therefrom is projected immediately into the street. BUSINESS DISTRICT is
defined as set forth in §
95.35;
      (2)   The unnecessary blowing or sounding of an automobile or other
vehicle horn or warning device; and/or
      (3)   The operation of a motor vehicle upon the street with the muffler
cutout open so that the exhaust does not go through the muffler.
(Ord. 213, passed 3-9-1931) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.05 NUISANCES GENERALLY.
   (A)   If any person, firm, company or corporation shall permit or suffer any
ground, building, ditch or other premises within the town, owned or occupied by
him, her or it, or of which he, she or it shall be the agent having charge of
the same, to become or be offensive, nauseous, hurtful or dangerous to the
neighborhood or travelers by reason of stagnant water, dead animals or from any
cause or causes, he, she or it shall be punished as hereinafter provided.
   (B)   If any person shall suffer any animal belonging to him or her or in
his or her charge, which may die of disease, or otherwise, to be in or upon any
street, alley or other grounds or place within the town limits, public or
private, for the space of 24 hours after the same shall have died, he or she
shall be punished as hereinafter provided.
   (C)   If any person shall allow to flow from any house, shop, factory,
stable, slaughterhouse or place, any foul or nauseous liquor or substance, of
any kind whatsoever, into or upon any adjacent ground or lot, or into any
street, alley or ditch within the town so as to be offensive, nauseous, hurtful
or dangerous; and any person who shall deposit in any such place any filth,
litter or refuse or carcass or thing so as to be offensive, nauseous, hurtful
or dangerous to any portion of the inhabitants of the town, he or she shall be
punished as hereafter provided.
   (D)   Except as hereinafter provided, it shall be and hereby is declared a
nuisance and misdemeanor to keep, operate, maintain or use a slaughterhouse or
to slaughter meat cattle, sheep or swine within the limits of the town;
provided, however, there is excluded, from this prohibition and it shall be
lawful to keep, operate, maintain and use slaughterhouses and to slaughter meat
cattle, sheep and swine in that area of the town lying east of the right-of-way
of Colorado & Southern Railway Company and north of the right-of-way of the
Elkhart & Santa Fe Railroad Company, upon condition that the slaughterhouses be
kept in a sanitary condition, that no offal or waste matter therefrom be
permitted to accumulate therein or thereby and that no offensive odors emanate
therefrom. Violation of the conditions or any of them shall render the
slaughterhouses a nuisance, subject to abatement as such, and their keeping,
operation maintenance or use a misdemeanor punishable as hereinafter provided.
(Ord. 12, passed 6-10-1908; Am. Ord. 279, passed 2-22-1940) Penalty, see §
96.99
Cross-reference:
   Cesspools, see also
Chapter 50 and §
52.005
   Nuisances, see also
Chapter 135
   Slaughterhouse wastes, see also §
52.051
   Slaughterhouses prohibited within town limits, see §
99.01
§ 96.06 JUNK, WEEDS AND RUBBISH ON VACANT AND NON-VACANT LOTS.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      NON-VACANT LOT. Any lot other than a vacant lot.
      RUBBISH. Trash and waste fragments, including, but not by way of
limitation, refuse, old rags, metals, rubber, glass parts of machines and
vehicles, waste paper, cloth, textiles, and old lumber having only salvage
value, and any and all other materials and junk having little or no value.
      VACANT LOT. Any lot which is not being used for dwelling or business
purposes and which is not being used as a junk yard as is authorized under §
94.01.
      WEEDS.  All vegetation allowed to grow to a height of 12 inches or more,
except for trees and cultivated, ornamental shrubs and flowers.
   (B)   It shall be the duty of all persons, firms, partnerships, and
corporations, who own vacant lots or non-vacant lots within the corporate
limits of the Town of Clayton, New Mexico, to keep the vacant lots or non-
vacant lots free and clear of all junk, weeds and rubbish.
   (C)   (1)   It shall be the duty of the Clerk-Treasurer of the Town of
Clayton, New Mexico, whenever it shall come to his or her attention that there
is junk and/or rubbish on a vacant lot or non-vacant lot or that a vacant lot
or non-vacant lot is overgrown with weeds, and the lot is within the corporate
limits of the Town of Clayton, New Mexico, to notify the owner of the lot,
asking him or her to remove the junk, rubbish and/or weeds.
      (2)   If, within 10 days of such notification, the owner has failed to
comply with the notice, the town shall clear the lot of the junk, rubbish and/
or weeds.
   (C)   Charges for the clearing of the lot and the removal of the junk,
rubbish and/or weeds by the Town of Clayton, New Mexico, shall constitute liens
upon the property so cleared, and shall be filed of record in the office of the
County Clerk of Union County, New Mexico. These liens shall be superior to all
other liens, except general property taxes and may be foreclosed in the manner
provided for by- law for the foreclosure of municipal assessment liens.
   (D)   In addition to or in lieu of the enforcement provisions of division
(C) above, in the event that a vacant lot or non-vacant lot is not in
compliance with the requirements of division (B), the owner of such lot may be
cited into Municipal Court, and upon being found by the Municipal Judge to be
guilty of the violation fined as set forth in §
96.99.
   (E)   This section is effective 30 days after passage.
(Ord. 572, passed 3-11-1991)
§ 96.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   (1)   Any person, association or corporation violating any of the
provisions of §
96.02 shall upon conviction be punished by fine in any amount not exceeding
$200 or imprisonment for any period not exceeding 60 days, or both the fine and
imprisonment, in the discretion of the court. Each day the nuisance is
maintained shall constitute a separate offense.
      (2)   The foregoing penal provisions shall not be so construed as to
prevent injunctive relief against anyone maintaining such a nuisance or
attempting or threatening to erect any prohibited toilet.
(Ord. 334, passed 9-12-1949)
   (C)   Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the provisions of §
96.03 shall upon conviction thereof be fined in any sum not exceeding $25 or
imprisoned for a term of not exceeding 10 days, or be punished by both the fine
and imprisonment in the discretion of the court.
(Ord. 292, passed 3-14-1944)
   (D)   Any person violating any of the provisions of §
96.04 shall, upon conviction, be punished by a fine in any amount not exceeding
$200, and each days violation shall be deemed a separate offense.
(Ord. 213, passed 3-9-1931)
   (E)   Violation of any of the provisions of §
96.05 shall be punishable by fine not exceeding $200 or imprisonment for a term
not exceeding 90 days, or by both the fine and imprisonment.
(Ord. 12, passed 6-10-1908; Am. Ord. 279, passed 2-22-1940)
   (F)   The owner of a lot in violation of the provisions of §
96.06 shall be fined in an amount not to exceed $300 and/or imprisoned for a
term not to exceed 60 days; for purposes of this section, each day in which a
lot is in violation shall be considered as a separate offense and may be cited
as such, and a penalty shall be imposed for each such offense.
(Ord. 572, passed 3-11-1991)
CHAPTER 97: HEALTH AND SANITATION
Section
Health
   
97.01   Inquire as to the sanitary condition of the town
   
97.02   Vaccines
   
97.03   Cleaning and quarantine
   
97.04   Certificate of cleaning and quarantine
   
97.05   Source of filth or cause of sickness on private property
   
97.06   Complying with Marshal
   
97.07   Deceased persons
   
97.08   Cause of death from certain diseases
   
97.09   Records of births and deaths
   
97.10   Records of births and deaths by parents and relatives
 
   
97.99   Penalty
HEALTH
§ 97.01 INQUIRE AS TO THE SANITARY CONDITION OF THE TOWN.
   The Board of Trustees of the town may from time to time make and establish
by ordinance, resolution or order those rules and regulations as they may deem
necessary, or as emergency may require, looking to the health and sanitary
condition of the community and town, the abatement of all nuisances tending to
endanger the public health, and the removal of all sources of filth and causes
of sickness, and it may take the steps as, in its judgment, are necessary to
restrain, stamp out or eradicate, check the progress of and isolate all
contagious diseases.
(Ord. 16, passed 6-18-1908)
§ 97.02 VACCINES.
   The Town Board of Trustees may, as often as it deems necessary, by order or
by resolution, require all persons within the corporate limits to be vaccinated
against small pox, and failure, neglect or refusal to do so will be deemed a
violation of this subchapter. Vaccine matter shall be provided at the cost of
the town, but each person shall bear the cost of his or her vaccination;
provided, however, if any person shall make affidavit that he or she is unable
to pay the cost, it shall be the duty of the Town Physician to vaccinate him or
her free of charge.
(Ord. 16, passed 6-18-1908)
§ 97.03 CLEANING AND QUARANTINE.
   All premises upon which any contagious disease has existed shall, upon the
order of the Town Physician, and under his or her direction, be thoroughly
cleansed and fumigated, and the quarantine provided in this section shall not
be raised, nor the placards of the premises be removed, until the same are
cleansed and fumigated as herein provided.
(Ord. 16, passed 6-18-1908)
§ 97.04 CERTIFICATE OF CLEANING AND QUARANTINE.
   When any contagious disease which has existed upon any premises in the town
has ceased to exist thereon and the premises have been thoroughly cleansed and
fumigated, as herein provided, it shall be the duty of the Town Physician to
deliver a certificate of the fact to the attending physician or to the owner or
occupant of the premises, which certificate shall be presented to the Town
Marshal, and thereupon the Town Marshal shall raise the quarantine, remove the
placards and file the certificate with the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
(Ord. 16, passed 6-18-1908)
§ 97.05 SOURCE OF FILTH OR CAUSE OF SICKNESS ON PRIVATE PROPERTY.
   Whenever any nuisance, source of filth or cause of sickness shall be found
on private property within the town, the Town Marshal shall order the owner or
occupant, or the person or persons who permit the conditions, to remove the
same within 24 hours, and any person who shall fail or refuse to obey the order
shall be deemed to have violated the provisions of this subchapter, and each
day the conditions shall remain shall be deemed to be a separate offense.
(Ord. 16, passed 6-18-1908)
§ 97.06 COMPLYING WITH MARSHAL.
   If the owners or occupants shall not comply with the order of the Marshal,
he or she may summon sufficient assistance and remove the source of filth and
cause of sickness, and if admittance to the premises is refused, the Marshal or
any person interested may make complaint before the Justice of the Peace,
stating the facts of the case, and the Justice of the Peace shall thereupon
issue a warrant to the Marshal commanding him or her to take sufficient aid and
between the hours of sunrise and sunset, to proceed to the place and remove the
nuisance, source of filth or cause of sickness, and the Town Physician may
attend and direct the Marshal in the service of the warrant.
(Ord. 16, passed 6-18-1908)
§ 97.07 DECEASED PERSONS.
   Every physician practicing medicine within the corporate limits of the Town
of Clayton shall within 24 hours after the death of any patient under his or
her charge report the same to the Town Physician, giving the name, age and
occupation of the deceased and the cause of the death, who shall thereupon
issue a permit of burial or transportation; and no undertaker or other person
shall bury or transport any corpse without the burial permit.
(Ord. 16, passed 6-18-1908)
§ 97.08 CAUSE OF DEATH FROM CERTAIN DISEASES.
   In case of deaths from smallpox, varioloid, diphtheria, membranous croup,
scarlet fever or measles, no public funeral shall be held aside from members of
the family, and no minor child shall attend the funeral.
(Ord. 16, passed 6-18-1908)
§ 97.09 RECORDS OF BIRTHS AND DEATHS.
   It shall be the duty of all physicians, nurses and midwives practicing
within the limits of the town to keep an accurate record of all births and
deaths occurring under their supervision, and upon the last day of each month
every physician, nurse or midwife shall file with the Town Physician a written
report of the birth or death; the reports shall be prepared upon blanks
furnished by the town, and in case of births shall give date of birth, sex of
child and name of the parents thereof; and in case of deaths shall give the
date of death and cause thereof, the name, age and occupation of the deceased.
(Ord. 16, passed 6-18-1908)
§ 97.10 RECORDS OF BIRTHS AND DEATHS BY PARENTS AND RELATIVES.
   In case of births and deaths where no physician, nurse or midwife is in
attendance, the report shall then be made by any parent or relative of the born
or deceased person, by any person in charge, or by anyone having knowledge of
the facts. Any person who shall fail to make the report required by the
preceding sections within 10 days of the date whereon the same is required to
be filed, shall be deemed to be guilty of a violation of this subchapter.
(Ord. 16, passed 6-18-1908) Penalty, see §
97.99
§ 97.99 PENALTY.
   Any person who violates any of the provisions of this chapter in any manner
shall be deemed to be guilty of a misdemeanor, and upon conviction thereof,
shall be fined in any sum not less than $5 nor more than $50, or by
imprisonment in the town or county jail for a period of not less than 5 days
nor more than 30 days, or both the fine and imprisonment by the discretion of
the court trying the case.
(Ord. 16, passed 6-18-1908)
CHAPTER 98: WEEDS
Section
   
98.01   Cutting of weeds
 
   
98.99   Penalty
Cross-reference:
   Additional provisions, weeds as nuisances, see §
135.02
§ 98.01 CUTTING OF WEEDS.
   (A)   Hereafter it shall be unlawful for any person or owner of real estate
within the corporate limits of the Town of Clayton, Union County, New Mexico,
to allow or maintain any rank growth of weeds over 12 inches in height on any
real estate.
   (B)   It shall be the duty of the owner of the real estate to cut and remove
any weeds from and after 10 days’ notice so to do by the Mayor, and notice to
the tenant on the property shall be notice to the owner; and if vacant, then
notice left placed on the property shall constitute proper notice.
   (C)   The term WEEDS in this section shall mean and include all rank growths
of vegetation which shall exhale or may exhale unpleasant or noxious odors, and
all high and rank vegetable growth that conceals or may conceal filthy
deposits.
(Ord. 134, passed - -)
§ 98.99 PENALTY.
   On the failure of the owner so to cut and remove the weeds after proper
notice thereof, the town may cut and remove the weeds and the cost thereof
shall be and remain a lien upon the property until paid, and in addition, the
owner may be punished, on conviction in the police court, by a fine of not less
than $5 not more than $10, or be confined in the jail for not less than 5 days
nor more than 10 days, or by both the fine and imprisonment.
(Ord. 134, passed - -)
